Ibn Abbas said: whoever thinks that God will never grant victory to Muhammad ﷺ in this world and the next, {let him extend a rope} that is, a cord, {toward the sky} meaning the ceiling of his house, {then let him cut it off}, meaning: then let him strangle himself with it. Mujahid, Ikrimah, Ata, Abu al-Jawza, Qatadah, and others said likewise.

Abd al-Rahman ibn Zayd ibn Aslam said: {let him extend a rope toward the sky} means: let him find a way to reach the sky, for victory only comes to Muhammad from the sky, {then let him cut} that off from himself, if he is able to do so.

The statement of Ibn Abbas and those who followed him is more fitting and clearer in meaning, and more forceful in its derision. For the meaning is: whoever thinks that God will not grant victory to Muhammad, his Book, and his religion, let him go and kill himself, if that is what enrages him, for God will surely grant him victory. God Most High said: {Indeed We will surely help Our messengers and those who believe, in the life of this world and on the Day when the witnesses will stand. The Day when their excuse will not benefit the wrongdoers, and for them is the curse and for them is the evil abode} [Ghafir: 51, 52]. This is why He said: {then let him see whether his scheming removes that which enrages him}

Al-Suddi said: meaning, from the affair of Muhammad ﷺ.

Ata al-Khurasani said: let him see whether that relieves what he finds of rage in his breast.

As for His saying, {And thus We sent it down}, meaning the Qur'an, {as clear signs}, meaning clear in their wording and their meaning, as a proof from God against the people, {and that God guides whom He wills}, meaning: He leads astray whom He wills and guides whom He wills, and His is the complete wisdom and the decisive proof in that. {He is not questioned about what He does, but they are questioned} [al-Anbiya: 23]. As for Him, this is due to His wisdom, His mercy, His justice, His knowledge, His dominance, and His majesty. There is no one who can overturn His judgment, and He is swift in reckoning.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ: مَنْ كَانَ يَظُنُّ أَنْ لَنْ يَنْصُرَ اللَّهُ مُحَمَّدًا ﷺ فِي الدُّنْيَا وَالْآخِرَةِ، ﴿فَلْيَمْدُدْ بِسَبَبٍ﴾ أَيْ: بِحَبْلٍ ﴿إِلَى السَّمَاءِ﴾ أَيْ: سَمَاءِ بَيْتِهِ، ﴿ثُمَّ ليَقْطَعْ﴾ يَقُولُ: ثُمَّ لِيَخْتَنِقْ بِهِ. وَكَذَا قَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ، وَعِكْرِمَةُ، وَعَطَاءٌ، وَأَبُو الْجَوْزَاءِ، وَقَتَادَةُ، وَغَيْرُهُمْ.

وَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ: ﴿فَلْيَمْدُدْ بِسَبَبٍ إِلَى السَّمَاءِ﴾ أَيْ: لِيَتَوَصَّلْ إِلَى بُلُوغِ السَّمَاءِ، فَإِنَّ النَّصْرَ إِنَّمَا يَأْتِي مُحَمَّدًا مِنَ السَّمَاءِ، ﴿ثُمَّ لِيَقْطَعْ﴾ ذَلِكَ عَنْهُ، إِنْ قَدَرَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ.

وَقَوْلُ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ وَأَصْحَابِهِ أَوْلَى وَأَظْهَرُ فِي الْمَعْنَى، وَأَبْلَغُ فِي التَّهَكُّمِ؛ فَإِنَّ الْمَعْنَى: مَنْ ظَنَّ أَنَّ اللَّهَ لَيْسَ بِنَاصِرٍ مُحَمَّدًا وَكِتَابَهُ وَدِينَهُ، فَلْيَذْهَبْ فَلْيَقْتُلْ نَفْسَهُ، إِنْ كَانَ ذَلِكَ غَائِظَهُ، فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ نَاصِرُهُ لَا مَحَالَةَ، قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: ﴿إِنَّا لَنَنْصُرُ رُسُلَنَا وَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا فِي الْحَيَاةِ الدُّنْيَا وَيَوْمَ يَقُومُ الأشْهَادُ. يَوْمَ لَا يَنْفَعُ الظَّالِمِينَ مَعْذِرَتُهُمْ وَلَهُمُ اللَّعْنَةُ وَلَهُمْ سُوءُ الدَّارِ﴾ [غَافِرٍ: ٥١، ٥٢] ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿فَلْيَنْظُرْ هَلْ يُذْهِبَنَّ كَيْدُهُ مَا يَغِيظُ﴾

قَالَ السُّدِّيُّ: يَعْنِي: مِنْ شَأْنِ مُحَمَّدٍ ﷺ.

وَقَالَ عَطَاءٌ الْخُرَاسَانِيُّ: فَلْيَنْظُرْ هَلْ يَشْفِي ذَلِكَ مَا يَجِدُ فِي صَدْرِهِ مِنَ الْغَيْظِ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَكَذَلِكَ أَنزلْنَاهُ﴾ أَيِ: الْقُرْآنَ ﴿آيَاتٍ بَيِّنَاتٍ﴾ أَيْ: وَاضِحَاتٍ فِي لَفْظِهَا وَمَعْنَاهَا، حُجَّةً مِنَ اللَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ ﴿وَأَنَّ اللَّهَ يَهْدِي مَنْ يُرِيدُ﴾ أَيْ: يُضِلُّ مَنْ يَشَاءُ، وَيَهْدِي مَنْ يَشَاءُ، وَلَهُ الْحِكْمَةُ التَّامَّةُ وَالْحُجَّةُ الْقَاطِعَةُ فِي ذَلِكَ، ﴿لَا يُسْأَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ وَهُمْ يُسْأَلُونَ﴾ [الْأَنْبِيَاءِ: ٢٣] ، أَمَّا هُوَ فَلِحِكْمَتِهِ وَرَحْمَتِهِ وَعَدْلِهِ، وَعِلْمِهِ وَقَهْرِهِ وَعَظَمَتِهِ، لَا مُعَقِّبَ لِحُكْمِهِ، وَهُوَ سَرِيعُ الْحِسَابِ.

---

## 22:17 — verse 17

### Translation

The Almighty informs about the followers of these various religions among the believers, and those besides them among the Jews and the Sabians (we have previously given the identification of them in Surat al-Baqarah, and the disagreement of the people concerning them), and the Christians and the Magians, and those who associated partners with God and worshipped others besides Him. Indeed, He, the Almighty, {will judge between them on the Day of Resurrection}, and He will decide between them with justice, admitting whoever believed in Him into Paradise, and whoever disbelieved in Him into the Fire. For He, the Almighty, is a witness over their deeds, a preserver of their words, knowing of their secrets and what their innermost hearts conceal.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يُخْبِرُ تَعَالَى عَنِ أَهْلِ هَذِهِ الْأَدْيَانِ الْمُخْتَلِفَةِ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ، وَمَنْ سِوَاهُمْ مِنَ الْيَهُودِ وَالصَّابِئِينَ -وَقَدْ قَدَّمْنَا فِي سُورَةِ "الْبَقَرَةِ" التَّعْرِيفَ بِهِمْ، واختلافَ النَّاسِ فِيهِمْ-وَالنَّصَارَى وَالْمَجُوسِ، وَالَّذِينَ أَشْرَكُوا فَعَبَدُوا غَيْرَ اللَّهِ مَعَهُ؛ فَإِنَّهُ تَعَالَى ﴿يَفْصِلُ بَيْنَهُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ﴾ ، وَيَحْكُمُ بَيْنَهُمْ بِالْعَدْلِ ، فَيُدْخِلُ مَنْ آمَنَ بِهِ الْجَنَّةَ، وَمَنْ كَفَرَ بِهِ النَّارَ، فَإِنَّهُ تَعَالَى شَهِيدٌ عَلَى أَفْعَالِهِمْ، حَفِيظٌ لِأَقْوَالِهِمْ، عليم بسرائرهم، وما تُكِن ضمائرهم.

---

## 22:18 — verse 18

### Translation

The Almighty informs that He alone is deserving of worship, having no partner, for everything prostrates to His greatness, willingly or unwillingly, and the prostration [of everything] is particular to it, as He said: {Have they not looked at what things God has created, how their shadows turn to the right and to the left, prostrating to God, and they are in humble submission?} [al-Nahl: 48]. And He said here: {Have you not seen that to God prostrates whoever is in the heavens and whoever is on the earth}, meaning: of the angels in the regions of the heavens, and the creatures in all directions, of mankind, jinn, beasts and birds, {and there is not a thing but glorifies Him with praise} [al-Isra: 44].

His statement, {and the sun and the moon and the stars}: He mentioned these specifically because they had been worshipped besides God, so He clarified that they prostrate to their Creator, and that they are lorded over and subjugated: {Do not prostrate to the sun or to the moon, but prostrate to God who created them, if it is Him you worship} [Fussilat: 37].

In the two Sahihs, from Abu Dharr, may God be pleased with him, he said: The Messenger of God ﷺ said, "Do you know where this sun goes?" I said, "God and His Messenger know best." He said, "It goes and prostrates beneath the Throne, then it seeks permission, and it is about to be said to it: Return from where you came."

In the Musnad and the Sunan of Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah, in the hadith of the eclipse: "The sun and the moon are two of God's creations, and they do not eclipse for anyone's death or life, but when God, Mighty and Majestic, manifests Himself to something of His creation, it becomes humbled before Him."

Abu al-'Aliyah said: There is no star in the sky, nor sun, nor moon, except that it falls prostrate to God when it sets, and it does not depart until it is given permission, whereupon it takes the right side until it returns to its place of rising.

As for the mountains and the trees, their prostration is by the turning of their shadows to the right and to the left. From Ibn 'Abbas, he said: A man came and said, "O Messenger of God, I saw myself last night in a dream as though I were praying behind a tree, and I prostrated, and the tree prostrated at my prostration, and I heard it saying: O God, record for me thereby a reward with You, and remove from me thereby a sin, and make it for me a treasure with You, and accept it from me as You accepted it from Your servant David." Ibn 'Abbas said: The Prophet ﷺ then recited a verse of prostration and prostrated, and I heard him saying the same thing that the man had reported the tree as saying.

Narrated by al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, and Ibn Hibban in his Sahih.

His statement, {and the moving creatures}, meaning: all animals.

It has come in a hadith from Imam Ahmad: that the Messenger of God ﷺ forbade taking the backs of riding animals as pulpits, for many a mount is better and more remembering of God than its rider.

His statement, {and many of the people}, meaning: prostrates to God willingly, by choice, worshipping thereby, {and many upon whom the punishment has been justified}, meaning: from among those who refused, declined, and were arrogant, {and whomever God humiliates, none can honor him; indeed God does what He wills}.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: [chain] from 'Ali, who said: It was said to 'Ali, "There is here a man who speaks concerning divine will (mashi'ah)." 'Ali said to him, "O servant of God, did God create you as He willed or as you willed?" He said, "Rather as He willed." He said, "Does He make you ill when He wills or when you will?" He said, "Rather when He wills." He said, "Does He heal you when He wills or when you will?" He said, "Rather when He wills." He said, "Does He admit you wherever you will or wherever He wills?" He said, "Rather wherever He wills." He said, "By God, had you said otherwise, I would have struck with the sword the place where your eyes are."

From Abu Hurayrah, he said: The Messenger of God ﷺ said: "When the son of Adam recites a verse of prostration, Satan withdraws weeping, saying: Woe to him! The son of Adam was commanded to prostrate and he prostrated, so Paradise is his; and I was commanded to prostrate and I refused, so the Fire is mine." Narrated by Muslim.

Imam Ahmad said: [chain] I heard 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir saying: I said, "O Messenger of God, has Surat al-Hajj been favored above the rest of the Qur'an with two prostrations?" He said, "Yes, and whoever does not prostrate at them, let him not recite them."

Narrated also by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi, from the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Lahi'ah, with the same chain. Al-Tirmidhi said, "It is not strong." But there is a consideration here, for Ibn Lahi'ah has explicitly stated that he heard it directly, and most of what was held against him was his practice of tadlis (concealing defects in transmission).

Abu Dawud said in al-Marasil: [chain] that the Messenger of God ﷺ said: "Surat al-Hajj has been favored over the Qur'an with two prostrations."

Then Abu Dawud said: This has been given a connected chain, meaning from a route other than this one, but it is not sound.

Al-Hafiz Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili said: [chain] that Abu al-Jahm reported: that 'Umar performed two prostrations in Surat al-Hajj while he was at al-Jabiyah, and said, "This surah has been favored with two prostrations."

Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah narrated, from the hadith of al-Harith ibn Sa'id al-'Utaqi, from 'Abdullah ibn Munayn, from 'Amr ibn al-'As: that the Messenger of God ﷺ taught him fifteen prostrations in the Qur'an, three of which are in al-Mufassal, and in Surat al-Hajj there are two prostrations. These are corroborating reports that strengthen one another.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يُخْبِرُ تَعَالَى أَنَّهُ الْمُسْتَحِقُّ لِلْعِبَادَةِ وَحْدَهُ لَا شَرِيكَ لَهُ، فَإِنَّهُ يَسْجُدُ لِعَظَمَتِهِ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ طَوْعًا وَكَرْهًا وَسُجُودُ [كُلِّ شَيْءٍ مِمَّا] يَخْتَصُّ بِهِ، كَمَا قَالَ: ﴿أَوَلَمْ يَرَوْا إِلَى مَا خَلَقَ اللَّهُ مِنْ شَيْءٍ يَتَفَيَّأُ ظِلالُهُ عَنِ الْيَمِينِ وَالشَّمَائِلِ سُجَّدًا لِلَّهِ وَهُمْ دَاخِرُونَ﴾ [النَّحْلِ: ٤٨] . وَقَالَ هَاهُنَا: ﴿أَلَمْ تَرَ أَنَّ اللَّهَ يَسْجُدُ لَهُ مَنْ فِي السَّمَاوَاتِ وَمَنْ فِي الأرْضِ﴾ أَيْ: مِنَ الْمَلَائِكَةِ فِي أَقْطَارِ السموات، وَالْحَيَوَانَاتِ فِي جَمِيعِ الْجِهَاتِ، مِنَ الْإِنْسِ وَالْجِنِّ وَالدَّوَابِّ وَالطَّيْرِ، ﴿وَإِنْ مِنْ شَيْءٍ إِلا يُسَبِّحُ بِحَمْدِهِ﴾ [الْإِسْرَاءِ: ٤٤] .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَالشَّمْسَ وَالْقَمَرَ وَالنُّجُومَ﴾ : إِنَّمَا ذَكَرَ هَذِهِ عَلَى التَّنْصِيصِ؛ لِأَنَّهَا قَدْ عُبدت مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ، فَبَيَّنَ أَنَّهَا تَسْجُدُ لِخَالِقِهَا، وَأَنَّهَا مَرْبُوبَةٌ مُسَخَّرَةٌ ﴿لَا تَسْجُدُوا لِلشَّمْسِ وَلا لِلْقَمَرِ وَاسْجُدُوا لِلَّهِ الَّذِي خَلَقَهُنَّ إِنْ كُنْتُمْ إِيَّاهُ تَعْبُدُونَ﴾ [فُصِّلَتْ: ٣٧] .

وَفِي الصَّحِيحَيْنِ عَنْ أَبِي ذَرٍّ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "أَتَدْرِي أَيْنَ تَذْهَبُ هَذِهِ الشَّمْسُ؟ ". قُلْتُ: اللَّهُ وَرَسُولُهُ أَعْلَمُ. قَالَ: "فَإِنَّهَا تَذْهَبُ فَتَسْجُدُ تَحْتَ الْعَرْشِ، ثُمَّ تُسْتَأْمَرُ فَيُوشِكُ أَنْ يُقَالَ لَهَا: ارْجِعِي مِنْ حَيْثُ جِئْتِ" .

وَفِي الْمُسْنَدِ وَسُنَنِ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، وَالنَّسَائِيِّ، وَابْنِ مَاجَهْ، فِي حَدِيثِ الْكُسُوفِ: "إِنَّ الشَّمْسَ وَالْقَمَرَ خَلْقان مِنْ خَلْق اللَّهِ، وَإِنَّهُمَا لَا يَنْكَسِفَانِ لِمَوْتِ أَحَدٍ وَلَا لِحَيَاتِهِ، وَلَكِنَّ اللَّهَ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ إِذَا تَجَلى لِشَيْءٍ مِنْ خَلْقِهِ خَشَعَ لَهُ" .

وَقَالَ أَبُو الْعَالِيَةِ: مَا فِي السَّمَاءِ نَجْمٌ وَلَا شَمْسٌ وَلَا قَمَرٌ، إِلَّا يَقَعُ لِلَّهِ سَاجِدًا حِينَ يَغِيبُ، ثُمَّ لَا يَنْصَرِفُ حَتَّى يُؤْذَنَ لَهُ، فَيَأْخُذَ ذَاتَ الْيَمِينِ حَتَّى يَرْجِعَ إِلَى مَطْلَعِهِ.

وَأَمَّا الْجِبَالُ وَالشَّجَرُ فَسُجُودُهُمَا بفَيء ظِلَالِهِمَا عَنِ الْيَمِينِ وَالشَّمَائِلِ: وَعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: جَاءَ رَجُلٌ فَقَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنِّي رَأَيْتُنِي اللَّيْلَةَ وَأَنَا نَائِمٌ، كَأَنِّي أُصَلِّي خَلْفَ شَجَرَةٍ، فسجدتُ فسجَدَت الشَّجَرَةُ لِسُجُودِي، فسمعتُها وَهِيَ تَقُولُ: اللَّهُمَّ، اكْتُبْ لِي بِهَا عِنْدَكَ أَجْرًا، وَضَعْ عَنِيَ بِهَا وِزْرًا، وَاجْعَلْهَا لِي عِنْدَكَ ذُخْرًا، وَتَقَبَّلْهَا مِنِّي كَمَا تَقَبَّلْتَهَا مِنْ عَبْدِكَ دَاوُدَ. قَالَ ابْنُ عباس: فقرأ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ سَجْدَةً ثُمَّ سَجَد، فَسَمِعْتُهُ وَهُوَ يقولُ مثلَ مَا أَخْبَرَهُ الرَّجُلُ عَنْ قَوْلِ الشَّجَرَةِ.

رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ، وَابْنُ مَاجَهْ، وَابْنُ حِبَّانَ فِي صَحِيحِهِ .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَالدَّوَابُّ﴾ أَيِ: الْحَيَوَانَاتُ كُلُّهَا.

وَقَدْ جَاءَ فِي الْحَدِيثِ عَنِ الْإِمَامِ أَحْمَدَ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ نَهَى عَنِ اتِّخَاذِ ظُهُورِ الدَّوَابِّ مَنَابِرَ فَرُبَّ مَرْكُوبَةٍ خَيْرٌ وَأَكْثَرُ ذِكْرًا لِلَّهِ مِنْ رَاكِبِهَا.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَكَثِيرٌ مِنَ النَّاسِ﴾ أَيْ: يَسْجُدُ لِلَّهِ طَوْعًا مُخْتَارًا مُتَعَبِّدًا بِذَلِكَ، ﴿وَكَثِيرٌ حَقَّ عَلَيْهِ الْعَذَابُ﴾ أَيْ: مِمَّنِ امْتَنَعَ وَأَبَى وَاسْتَكْبَرَ، ﴿وَمَنْ يُهِنِ اللَّهُ فَمَا لَهُ مِنْ مُكْرِمٍ إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَفْعَلُ مَا يَشَاءُ﴾ .

وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا أَحْمَدُ بْنُ شَيْبَانَ الرَّمْلِيُّ، حَدَّثَنَا الْقَدَّاحُ، عَنْ جَعْفَرِ بْنِ مُحَمَّدٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ عَلِيٍّ قَالَ: قِيلَ لَعَلِّيٍّ: إِنَّ هَاهُنَا رَجُلًا يَتَكَلَّمُ فِي الْمَشِيئَةِ. فَقَالَ لَهُ عَلِيٌّ: يَا عَبْدَ اللَّهِ، خَلَقَكَ اللَّهُ كَمَا يَشَاءُ أَوْ كَمَا شِئْتَ ؟ قَالَ: بَلْ كَمَا شَاءَ. قَالَ: فَيُمَرِّضُكَ إِذَا شَاءَ أَوْ إِذَا شِئْتَ؟ قَالَ: بَلْ إِذَا شَاءَ. قَالَ: فَيَشْفِيكَ إِذَا شَاءَ أَوْ إِذَا شِئْتَ؟ قَالَ: بَلْ إِذَا شَاءَ. قَالَ: فَيُدْخِلُكَ حَيْثُ شِئْتَ أَوْ حَيْثُ يَشَاءُ؟ قَالَ: بَلْ حَيْثُ يَشَاءُ. قَالَ: وَاللَّهِ لَوْ قُلْتَ غَيْرَ ذَلِكَ لضربتُ الَّذِي فِيهِ عَيْنَاكَ بِالسَّيْفِ.

وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "إِذَا قَرَأَ ابنُ آدَمَ السَّجْدَةَ اعْتَزَلَ الشَّيْطَانُ يَبْكِي يَقُولُ: يَا وَيْلَهُ. أُمِرَ ابْنُ آدَمَ بِالسُّجُودِ فَسَجَدَ، فَلَهُ الْجَنَّةُ، وأمِرتُ بِالسُّجُودِ فأبيتُ، فَلِيَ النَّارُ" رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ .

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو سَعِيدٍ مَوْلَى بَنِي هَاشِمٍ وَأَبُو عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ الْمُقْرِئُ قَالَا حَدَّثَنَا ابْنُ لَهِيعة، حَدَّثَنَا مَشْرَح بْنُ هَاعَانَ أَبُو مُصعب الْمُعَافِرِيُّ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ عُقَبَةَ بْنَ عَامِرٍ يَقُولُ: قُلْتُ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، أَفُضِّلَتْ سُورَةُ الْحَجِّ عَلَى سَائِرِ الْقُرْآنِ بِسَجْدَتَيْنِ؟ قَالَ: "نَعَمْ، فَمَنْ لَمْ يَسْجُدْ بِهِمَا فَلَا يَقْرَأْهُمَا".

وَرَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ وَالتِّرْمِذِيُّ، مِنْ حَدِيثِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ لَهِيعَةَ، بِهِ . وَقَالَ التِّرْمِذِيُّ: "لَيْسَ بِقَوِيٍّ " وَفِي هَذَا نَظَرٌ؛ فَإِنَّ ابْنَ لَهِيعة قَدْ صَرح فِيهِ بِالسَّمَاعِ، وَأَكْثَرُ مَا نَقَموا عَلَيْهِ تدليسه.

وَقَدْ قَالَ أَبُو دَاوُدَ فِي الْمَرَاسِيلِ: حَدَّثَنَا أَحْمَدُ بْنُ عَمْرِو بْنِ السَّرح، أَنْبَأَنَا ابْنُ وَهْب، أَخْبَرَنِي مُعَاوِيَةُ بْنُ صَالِحٍ، عَنْ عَامِرِ بْنِ جَشِب ، عَنْ خَالِدِ بْنِ مَعْدان؛ أَنَّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: "فُضِّلت سُورَةُ الْحَجِّ عَلَى الْقُرْآنِ بِسَجْدَتَيْنِ".

ثُمَّ قَالَ أَبُو دَاوُدَ: وَقَدْ أسندَ هَذَا، يَعْنِي: مِنْ غَيْرِ هَذَا الْوَجْهِ، وَلَا يَصِحُّ .

وَقَالَ الْحَافِظُ أَبُو بَكْرٍ الْإِسْمَاعِيلِيُّ: حَدَّثَنَا ابْنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، حَدَّثَنَا يَزِيدُ بْنُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، حَدَّثَنَا الْوَلِيدُ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو عَمْرٍو، حَدَّثَنَا حَفْصُ بْنُ عَنَانٍ، حَدَّثَنِي نَافِعٌ، حَدَّثَنِي أَبُو الْجَهْمِ: أَنَّ عُمَرَ سَجَدَ سَجْدَتَيْنِ فِي الْحَجِّ، وَهُوَ بِالْجَابِيَةِ، وَقَالَ: إِنَّ هَذِهِ فُضِّلَتْ بِسَجْدَتَيْنِ .

وَرَوَى أَبُو دَاوُدَ وَابْنُ مَاجَهْ، مِنْ حَدِيثِ الْحَارِثِ بْنِ سَعِيدٍ العُتَقيّ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مُنَين، عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ الْعَاصِ؛ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ أَقْرَأَهُ خَمْسَ عَشْرَةَ سَجْدَةً فِي الْقُرْآنِ، مِنْهَا ثَلَاثٌ فِي المُفَصّل، وَفِي سُورَةِ الْحَجِّ سَجْدَتَانِ . فَهَذِهِ شَوَاهِدُ يَشُدّ بَعْضُهَا بَعْضًا.

---

## 22:19-22 — verses 19-22 (shared commentary)

### Translation

It is established in the two Sahihs, from the hadith of Abu Mijlaz, from Qays ibn Ubad, from Abu Dharr, that he used to swear an oath that this verse, {These are two adversaries who disputed concerning their Lord}, was revealed concerning Hamzah and his two companions, and Utbah and his two companions, on the day they went out to fight each other at Badr.

This is the wording of al-Bukhari in his explanation of it. Then al-Bukhari said:

Al-Hajjaj ibn al-Minhal told us, al-Mu'tamir ibn Sulayman told us, I heard my father, Abu Mijlaz told us, from Qays ibn Ubad, from Ali ibn Abi Talib, that he said: I am the first to kneel before the Merciful for judgment on the Day of Resurrection. Qays said: and it was concerning them that {These are two adversaries who disputed concerning their Lord} was revealed. He said: they are the ones who dueled on the day of Badr: Ali, Hamzah, and Ubaydah, and Shaybah ibn Rabi'ah, Utbah ibn Rabi'ah, and al-Walid ibn Utbah. Al-Bukhari alone transmitted this.

Sa'id ibn Abi Arubah said, from Qatadah, concerning His saying: {These are two adversaries who disputed concerning their Lord}, he said: the Muslims and the People of the Book disputed. The People of the Book said: our prophet came before your prophet, and our book before your book, so we have a greater claim to God than you. And the Muslims said: our book supersedes all other books, and our prophet is the seal of the prophets, so we have a greater claim to God than you. So God gave Islam victory over those who opposed it, and revealed: {These are two adversaries who disputed concerning their Lord}. Al-Awfi likewise narrated this from Ibn Abbas.

Shu'bah said, from Qatadah, concerning His saying: {These are two adversaries who disputed concerning their Lord}, he said: one who affirms the truth and one who denies it.

Ibn Abi Najih said, from Mujahid, concerning this verse: it is the likeness of the disbeliever and the believer, who dispute concerning the resurrection. And he said, in another report, he and Ata, concerning this verse: they are the believers and the disbelievers.

The statement of Mujahid and Ata, that what is meant by this are the disbelievers and the believers, encompasses all the other statements, and includes within it the story of the day of Badr and other than it. For the believers wanted the support of God's religion, while the disbelievers wanted to extinguish the light of faith, to bring down the truth, and to make falsehood prevail. This is the choice of Ibn Jarir, and it is a good one. This is why He said: {As for those who disbelieved, garments of fire have been cut out for them}, meaning: garments cut from fire have been fashioned for them in detail.

Sa'id ibn Jubayr said: of copper, which is the hottest of things when heated.

{Scalding water will be poured over their heads. By which whatever is in their bellies will be melted, and their skins as well}, meaning: when scalding water is poured on their heads, it being water at the utmost degree of heat.

Sa'id ibn Jubayr said: it is molten copper, which melts whatever is in their bellies of fat and intestines. This was said by Ibn Abbas, Mujahid, Sa'id ibn Jubayr, and others. Likewise their skins melt. Ibn Abbas and Sa'id said: they fall away.

Ibn Jarir said: Muhammad ibn al-Muthanna told me, Ibrahim Abu Ishaq al-Talaqani told us, Ibn al-Mubarak told us, from Sa'id ibn Zayd, from Abu al-Samh, from Ibn Hujayrah, from Abu Hurayrah, from the Prophet ﷺ, who said: "Indeed the scalding water is poured upon their heads, and it penetrates the skull until it reaches his inward parts, and it strips away what is in his inward parts until it reaches his feet, and that is the melting (al-sahr), then he is restored as he was."

Al-Tirmidhi narrated it from the hadith of Ibn al-Mubarak, and said: hasan sahih (good and authentic). Ibn Abi Hatim likewise narrated it, from his father, from Abu Nu'aym, from Ibn al-Mubarak, with the same chain. Then Ibn Abi Hatim said:

Ali ibn al-Husayn told us, Ahmad ibn Abi al-Hawari told us, I heard Abdullah ibn al-Surri say: the angel comes to him carrying the vessel with two tongs because of its heat, and when he brings it close to his face he recoils from it. He said: then he raises a mace (miqma'ah) that he has with him and strikes him on the head with it, so his brain pours out, then the vessel of his brain is emptied out, and it reaches his inward parts by way of his brain. That is the meaning of His saying: {By which whatever is in their bellies will be melted, and their skins as well}.

Concerning His saying: {And for them are maces of iron}, Imam Ahmad said:

Hasan ibn Musa told us, Ibn Lahi'ah told us, Darraj told us, from Abu al-Haytham, from Abu Sa'id, from the Messenger of God ﷺ, who said: "If a mace of iron were placed on the earth, and jinn and mankind gathered together for it, they would not be able to lift it from the earth."

Imam Ahmad also said: Musa ibn Dawud told us, Ibn Lahi'ah told us, Darraj told us, from Abu al-Haytham, from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, who said: the Messenger of God ﷺ said: "If a mountain were struck with a mace of iron, it would crumble, then it would return as it was. And if a bucket of ghassaq (foul discharge) were poured out in this world, it would make the people of this world stink."

Ibn Abbas said, concerning His saying: {And for them are maces of iron}: they are struck with them, and every limb falls in its place, and they cry out for destruction.

Concerning His saying: {Whenever they want to come out of it, from anguish, they are returned into it}: al-A'mash said, from Abu Zibyan, from Salman, who said: the fire is black, dark, its flame does not give light nor does its ember. Then he recited: {Whenever they want to come out of it, from anguish, they are returned into it}.

Zayd ibn Aslam said, concerning this verse: {Whenever they want to come out of it, from anguish, they are returned into it}: it has reached me that the people of the fire, in the fire, do not breathe.

Al-Fudayl ibn Iyad said: by God, they do not even hope to get out. Indeed their legs are shackled and their hands are bound, but its flame lifts them up, and its maces drive them back.

Concerning His saying: {And taste the punishment of the burning}, this is like His saying: {And it will be said to them, taste the punishment of the fire which you used to deny} [al-Sajdah: 20]. The meaning of the statement is that they are humiliated by the punishment, in word and in deed.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

ثَبَتَ فِي الصَّحِيحَيْنِ، مِنْ حَدِيثِ أَبِي مِجْلَز، عَنْ قَيْسِ بْنِ عُبَاد، عَنِ أَبِي ذَرٍّ؛ أَنَّهُ كَانَ يُقْسِمُ قَسَمًا أَنَّ هَذِهِ الْآيَةَ: ﴿هَذَانِ خَصْمَانِ اخْتَصَمُوا فِي رَبِّهِمْ﴾ نَزَلَتْ فِي حَمْزَةَ وصاحِبَيه، وعتبةَ وَصَاحِبَيْهِ، يَوْمَ بَرَزُوا فِي بَدْرٍ .

لَفْظُ الْبُخَارِيِّ عِنْدَ تَفْسِيرِهَا، ثُمَّ قَالَ الْبُخَارِيُّ:

حَدَّثَنَا الْحَجَّاجُ بْنُ مِنْهَال، حَدَّثَنَا الْمُعْتَمِرُ بْنُ سُلَيْمَانَ، سَمِعْتُ أَبِي، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو مِجْلز عَنْ قَيْسِ بْنِ عُبَاد، عَنْ عَلِيِّ بْنِ أَبِي طَالِبٍ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: أَنَا أَوَّلُ مَنْ يَجثُو بَيْنَ يَدَيِ الرَّحْمَنِ لِلْخُصُومَةِ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ. قَالَ قَيْسٌ: وَفِيهِمْ نَزَلَتْ: ﴿هَذَانِ خَصْمَانِ اخْتَصَمُوا فِي رَبِّهِمْ﴾ ، قَالَ: هُمُ الَّذِينَ بَارَزُوا يَوْمَ بَدْرٍ: عليّ وحمزة وعبيدة، وشيبة ابن رَبِيعَةَ وَعُتْبَةُ بْنُ رَبِيعَةَ وَالْوَلِيدُ بْنُ عُتْبَةَ. انْفَرَدَ بِهِ الْبُخَارِيُّ .

وَقَالَ سَعِيدُ بْنُ أَبِي عَرُوبة، عَنْ قَتَادَةَ فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿هَذَانِ خَصْمَانِ اخْتَصَمُوا فِي رَبِّهِمْ﴾ قَالَ: اخْتَصَمَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ وَأَهْلُ الْكِتَابِ، فَقَالَ أَهْلُ الْكِتَابِ: نَبِيُّنَا قَبْلَ نَبِيِّكُمْ، وَكِتَابُنَا قبل كتابكم. فنحن أولى بالله مِنْكُمْ. وَقَالَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ: كِتَابُنَا يَقْضِي عَلَى الْكُتُبِ كُلِّهَا، وَنَبِيُّنَا خَاتَمُ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ، فَنَحْنُ أَوْلَى بِاللَّهِ مِنْكُمْ. فَأَفْلَجَ اللَّهُ الإسلامَ عَلَى مَنْ نَاوَأَهُ، وَأَنْزَلَ: ﴿هَذَانِ خَصْمَانِ اخْتَصَمُوا فِي رَبِّهِمْ﴾ . وَكَذَا رَوَى العَوفي، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ.

وَقَالَ شُعْبَةُ، عَنْ قَتَادَةَ فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿هَذَانِ خَصْمَانِ اخْتَصَمُوا فِي رَبِّهِمْ﴾ قَالَ: مُصدق وَمُكَذِّبٌ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي نَجِيح، عَنْ مُجَاهِدٍ فِي هَذِهِ الْآيَةِ: مَثَلُ الْكَافِرِ وَالْمُؤْمِنِ اخْتَصَمَا فِي الْبَعْثِ. وَقَالَ -فِي رِوَايَةٍ: هُوَ وَعَطَاءٌ فِي هَذِهِ الْآيَةِ-: هُمُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ وَالْكَافِرُونَ.

وَقَالَ عِكْرِمَةُ: ﴿هَذَانِ خَصْمَانِ اخْتَصَمُوا فِي رَبِّهِمْ﴾ قَالَ: هِيَ الْجَنَّةُ وَالنَّارُ، قَالَتِ النَّارَ: اجْعَلْنِي لِلْعُقُوبَةِ، وَقَالَتِ الْجَنَّةُ: اجْعَلْنِي لِلرَّحْمَةِ.

وقولُ مُجَاهِدٍ وَعَطَاءٍ: إِنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِهَذِهِ الْكَافِرُونَ وَالْمُؤْمِنُونَ، يَشْمَلُ الْأَقْوَالَ كُلَّهَا، وَيَنْتَظِمُ فِيهِ قِصَّةُ يَوْمِ بَدْرٍ وَغَيْرُهَا؛ فَإِنَّ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ يُرِيدُونَ نُصْرَةَ دِينِ اللَّهِ، وَالْكَافِرُونَ يُرِيدُونَ إِطْفَاءَ نُورِ الْإِيمَانِ وخذلانَ الْحَقِّ وَظُهُورَ الْبَاطِلِ. وَهَذَا اخْتِيَارُ ابْنِ جَرِيرٍ، وَهُوَ حَسَن؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿فَالَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا قُطِّعَتْ لَهُمْ ثِيَابٌ مِنْ نَارٍ﴾ أَيْ: فُصِّلَتْ لَهُمْ مُقَطَّعَاتٌ مِنْ نَارٍ.

قَالَ سَعِيدُ بْنُ جُبَيْرٍ: مِنْ نُحَاسٍ وَهُوَ أَشَدُّ الْأَشْيَاءِ حَرَارَةً إِذَا حَمِيَ.

﴿يُصَبُّ مِنْ فَوْقِ رُءُوسِهِمُ الْحَمِيمُ. يُصْهَرُ بِهِ مَا فِي بُطُونِهِمْ وَالْجُلُودُ﴾ أَيْ: إِذَا صُبَّ عَلَى رُءُوسِهِمُ الْحَمِيمُ، وَهُوَ الْمَاءُ الْحَارُّ فِي غَايَةِ الْحَرَارَةِ.

وَقَالَ سَعِيدُ [بْنُ جُبَيْرٍ] هُوَ النُّحَاسُ الْمُذَابُ، أَذَابَ مَا فِي بُطُونِهِمْ مِنَ الشَّحْمِ وَالْأَمْعَاءِ. قَالَهُ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ، وَمُجَاهِدٌ، وَسَعِيدُ بْنُ جُبَيْرٍ، وَغَيْرُهُمْ. وَكَذَلِكَ تَذُوبُ جُلُودُهُمْ، وَقَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ وَسَعِيدٌ: تَسَاقَطَ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنِي مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ الْمُثَنَّى، حَدَّثَنَا إِبْرَاهِيمُ أَبُو إِسْحَاقَ الطالَقاني، حَدَّثَنَا ابْنُ الْمُبَارَكِ عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ زَيْدٍ ، عَنِ أَبِي السَّمْح، عَنِ ابْنِ حُجَيرة، عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيرة، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عليه وسلم قال: "إِنْ الْحَمِيمَ ليُصَب عَلَى رُءُوسِهِمْ، فينفُد الجمجمةَ حَتَّى يَخْلُصَ إِلَى جَوْفِهِ، فَيَسْلِتُ مَا فِي جَوْفِهِ، حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ قَدَمَيْهِ، وَهُوَ الصِّهْرُ، ثُمَّ يُعَادُ كَمَا كَانَ".

وَرَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ مِنْ حَدِيثِ ابْنِ الْمُبَارَكِ ، وَقَالَ: حَسَنٌ صَحِيحٌ. وَهَكَذَا رَوَاهُ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ أَبِي نُعَيْمٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ الْمُبَارَكِ، بِهِ ثُمَّ قَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ:

حَدَّثَنَا عَلِيُّ بْنُ الْحُسَيْنِ، حَدَّثَنَا أَحْمَدُ بْنُ أَبِي الحَوَاريّ، سَمِعْتُ عَبْدَ الله ابن السُّرِّيّ قَالَ: يَأْتِيهِ الْمَلَكُ يَحْمِلُ الْإِنَاءَ بِكَلْبتين مِنْ حَرَارَتِهِ، فَإِذَا أَدْنَاهُ مِنْ وَجْهِهِ تَكَرَّهَهُ، قال: فيرفع مِقْمَعَة معه فيضرب بِهَا رَأْسَهُ، فَيُفرغ دِمَاغَهُ، ثُمَّ يُفرغ الْإِنَاءَ مِنْ دِمَاغِهِ، فَيَصِلُ إِلَى جَوْفِهِ مِنْ دِمَاغِهِ، فَذَلِكَ قَوْلُهُ: ﴿يُصْهَرُ بِهِ مَا فِي بُطُونِهِمْ وَالْجُلُودُ﴾

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَلَهُمْ مَقَامِعُ مِنْ حَدِيدٍ﴾ ، قَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ:

حَدَّثَنَا حَسَنُ بْنُ مُوسَى، حَدَّثَنَا ابْنُ لَهِيعة، حَدَّثَنَا دَرَّاج، عَنْ أَبِي الْهَيْثَمِ، عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ، عَنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَالَ: "لَوْ أَنَّ مِقْمَعا مِن حَديد وُضِع فِي الْأَرْضِ، فَاجْتَمَعَ لَهُ الثَّقَلَانِ مَا أقَلُّوه مِنَ الْأَرْضِ" .

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا مُوسَى بْنُ دَاوُدَ، حَدَّثَنَا ابْنُ لَهِيعة، حَدَّثَنَا دَرَّاج، عَنْ أَبِي الْهَيْثَمِ، عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "لَوْ ضُرب الجبلُ بمِقْمَع مِنْ حَدِيدٍ، لَتَفَتَّتَ ثُمَّ عَادَ كَمَا كَانَ، وَلَوْ أَنَّ دَلْوًا مِنْ غَسَّاق يُهَرَاق فِي الدُّنْيَا لَأَنْتَنَ أَهْلُ الدُّنْيَا" .

وَقَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَلَهُمْ مَقَامِعُ مِنْ حَدِيدٍ﴾ قَالَ: يُضْرَبُونَ بِهَا، فَيَقَعُ كُلُّ عُضْوٍ عَلَى حِيَالِهِ، فَيَدْعُونَ بِالثُّبُورِ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿كُلَّمَا أَرَادُوا أَنْ يَخْرُجُوا مِنْهَا مِنْ غَمٍّ أُعِيدُوا فِيهَا﴾ : قَالَ الْأَعْمَشُ، عَنِ أَبِي ظِبْيان، عَنْ سَلْمَانَ قَالَ: النَّارُ سَوْدَاءُ مُظْلِمَةٌ، لَا يُضِيءُ لَهَبُهَا وَلَا جَمْرُهَا، ثُمَّ قَرَأَ: ﴿كُلَّمَا أَرَادُوا أَنْ يَخْرُجُوا مِنْهَا مِنْ غَمٍّ أُعِيدُوا فِيهَا﴾

وَقَالَ زَيْدُ بْنُ أَسْلَمَ فِي هَذِهِ الْآيَةِ: ﴿كُلَّمَا أَرَادُوا أَنْ يَخْرُجُوا مِنْهَا مِنْ غَمٍّ أُعِيدُوا فِيهَا﴾ قَالَ: بَلَغَنِي أَنَّ أَهْلَ النَّارِ فِي النَّارِ لَا يَتَنَفَّسُونَ.

وَقَالَ الفُضيل بْنُ عِيَاضٍ: وَاللَّهِ مَا طَمِعُوا فِي الْخُرُوجِ، إِنَّ الْأَرْجُلَ لَمُقَيَّدَةٌ، وَإِنَّ الْأَيْدِيَ لَمُوثَقَةٌ، وَلَكِنْ يَرْفَعُهُمْ لَهَبُهَا، وَتَرُدُّهُمْ مَقَامِعُهَا.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَذُوقُوا عَذَابَ الْحَرِيقِ﴾ كَقَوْلِهِ ﴿وَقِيلَ لَهُمْ ذُوقُوا عَذَابَ النَّارِ الَّذِي كُنْتُمْ بِهِ تُكَذِّبُونَ﴾ [السَّجْدَةِ: ٢٠] وَمَعْنَى الْكَلَامِ: أَنَّهُمْ يُهَانُونَ بِالْعَذَابِ قَوْلًا وَفِعْلًا.

---

## 22:23-24 — verses 23-24 (shared commentary)

### Translation

When the Exalted informed of the state of the people of the Fire, we seek refuge in Allah from their state, and of the punishment, chastisement, burning, and shackles they are in, and of the garments of fire prepared for them, He mentioned the state of the people of Paradise, we ask Allah out of His bounty and generosity to admit us into Paradise, and He said: {Indeed, Allah admits those who believe and do righteous deeds into Gardens beneath which rivers flow}, meaning: they wind through their surroundings, their expanses, and their sides, and beneath their trees and palaces, and they direct them wherever they wish and to whatever place they wish. {They are adorned therein} with ornaments, {they are adorned therein with bracelets of gold and pearls}, meaning: on their hands, as the Prophet ﷺ said in the hadith agreed upon [by Bukhari and Muslim]: "The ornament will reach on the believer to wherever the water of wudu reaches."

Ka'b al-Ahbar said: In Paradise there is an angel, if I wished to name him I would name him, who has been fashioning ornaments for the people of Paradise since Allah created him until the Day of Resurrection. If a single link of it were brought forth, meaning a bracelet from it, it would repel the rays of the sun just as the sun repels the light of the moon.

His saying: {and their garment therein is silk}: in contrast to the garments of the people of the Fire which were cut out for them, the garment of these is of silk, its heavy brocade (istabraq) and its fine silk (sundus), as He said: {Upon them will be green garments of fine silk and heavy brocade, and they will be adorned with bracelets of silver, and their Lord will give them a pure drink to drink. Indeed this is for you a reward, and your effort has been appreciated} [al-Insan: 21-22]. And in the Sahih: "Do not wear silk or dibaj (silk brocade) in this world, for whoever wears it in this world will not wear it in the Hereafter."

Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr said: Whoever does not wear silk in the Hereafter has not entered Paradise. Allah the Exalted said: {and their garment therein is silk}.

His saying: {and they were guided to the good speech} is like His saying: {And those who believed and did righteous deeds were admitted into Gardens beneath which rivers flow, abiding therein by the permission of their Lord, their greeting therein being: peace} [Ibrahim: 23], and His saying: {And the angels will enter upon them from every gate: peace be upon you for what you patiently endured, and excellent is the final abode} [al-Ra'd: 23-24], and His saying: {They will not hear therein any vain talk or sin, only the saying: peace, peace} [al-Waqi'ah: 25-26]. So they were guided to the place where they hear good speech, {and they are received therein with greeting and peace} [al-Furqan: 75], unlike how the people of the Fire are humiliated with speech that terrifies them and reproaches them, when it is said to them: {and taste the punishment of the burning}.

His saying: {and they were guided to the path of the Praiseworthy One (al-Hamid)} means: to the place where they praise their Lord for the good He did to them, the blessings He bestowed upon them, and what He conferred on them, as has come in the Sahih: "They will be inspired to glorify and praise, just as they are inspired to breathe."

Some of the commentators said regarding His saying: {and they were guided to the good speech}, meaning: the Qur'an. And it was said: "There is no god but Allah." And it was said: the prescribed remembrances (adhkar). {and they were guided to the path of the Praiseworthy One} meaning: the straight path in this world. All of this does not contradict what we have mentioned. And Allah knows best.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

لَمَّا أَخْبَرَ تَعَالَى عَنْ حَالِ أَهْلِ النَّارِ، عِيَاذًا بِاللَّهِ مِنْ حَالِهِمْ، وَمَا هُمْ فِيهِ مِنَ الْعَذَابِ والنَّكال وَالْحَرِيقِ وَالْأَغْلَالِ، وَمَا أُعِدَّ لَهُمْ مِنَ الثِّيَابِ مِنَ النَّارِ، ذَكَرَ حَالَ أَهْلِ الْجَنَّةِ -نَسْأَلُ اللَّهُ مِنْ فَضْلِهِ وَكَرَمِهِ أَنْ يُدْخِلَنَا الْجَنَّةَ-فَقَالَ: ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ يُدْخِلُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ جَنَّاتٍ تَجْرِي مِنْ تَحْتِهَا الأنْهَارُ﴾ أَيْ: تتخَرّق فِي أَكْنَافِهَا وَأَرْجَائِهَا وَجَوَانِبِهَا، وَتَحْتَ أَشْجَارِهَا وَقُصُورِهَا، يَصْرِفُونَهَا حَيْثُ شَاءُوا وَأَيْنَ شَاءُوا، ﴿يُحَلَّوْنَ فِيهَا﴾ مِنَ الْحِلْيَةِ، ﴿يُحَلَّوْنَ فِيهَا مِنْ أَسَاوِرَ مِنْ ذَهَبٍ وَلُؤْلُؤًا﴾ أَيْ: فِي أَيْدِيهِمْ، كَمَا قَالَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ فِي الْحَدِيثِ الْمُتَّفِقِ عَلَيْهِ: "تَبْلُغُ الحِلْيَة مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِ حَيْثُ يَبْلُغُ الوُضُوء" .

وَقَالَ كَعْبُ الْأَحْبَارِ: إِنَّ فِي الْجَنَّةِ مَلَكًا لَوْ شِئْتُ أَنْ أُسَمِّيَهُ لسميتُه، يَصُوغُ لِأَهْلِ الْجَنَّةِ الْحُلِيَّ مُنْذُ خَلَقَهُ اللَّهُ إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ، لَوْ أُبْرِزَ قُلْب مِنْهَا -أَيْ: سِوَارٌ مِنْهَا-لَرَدَّ شُعَاعَ الشَّمْسِ، كَمَا تَرُدُّ الشَّمْسُ نُورَ الْقَمَرِ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَلِبَاسُهُمْ فِيهَا حَرِيرٌ﴾ : فِي مُقَابَلَةِ ثِيَابِ أَهْلِ النَّارِ الَّتِي فُصِّلَتْ لَهُمْ، لِبَاسُ هَؤُلَاءِ مِنَ الْحَرِيرِ، إِسْتَبْرَقِهِ وسُنْدُسه، كَمَا قَالَ: ﴿عَالِيَهُمْ ثِيَابُ سُنْدُسٍ خُضْرٌ وَإِسْتَبْرَقٌ وَحُلُّوا أَسَاوِرَ مِنْ فِضَّةٍ وَسَقَاهُمْ رَبُّهُمْ شَرَابًا طَهُورًا. إِنَّ هَذَا كَانَ لَكُمْ جَزَاءً وَكَانَ سَعْيُكُمْ مَشْكُورًا﴾ [الْإِنْسَانِ: ٢١، ٢٢] ، وَفِي الصَّحِيحِ: "لَا تَلْبَسُوا الْحَرِيرَ وَلَا الدِّيبَاجَ فِي الدُّنْيَا، فَإِنَّهُ مَنْ لَبِسَهُ فِي الدُّنْيَا لَمْ يَلْبَسْهُ فِي الْآخِرَةِ" .

قَالَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ الزُّبَيْرِ: وَمَنْ لَمْ يَلْبَسِ الْحَرِيرَ فِي الْآخِرَةِ، لَمْ يَدْخُلِ الْجَنَّةَ، قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَلِبَاسُهُمْ فِيهَا حَرِيرٌ﴾

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَهُدُوا إِلَى الطَّيِّبِ مِنَ الْقَوْلِ﴾ كَقَوْلِهِ ﴿وَأُدْخِلَ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ جَنَّاتٍ تَجْرِي مِنْ تَحْتِهَا الأنْهَارُ خَالِدِينَ فِيهَا بِإِذْنِ رَبِّهِمْ تَحِيَّتُهُمْ فِيهَا سَلامٌ﴾ [إِبْرَاهِيمَ: ٢٣] ، وَقَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَالْمَلائِكَةُ يَدْخُلُونَ عَلَيْهِمْ مِنْ كُلِّ بَابٍ. سَلامٌ عَلَيْكُمْ بِمَا صَبَرْتُمْ فَنِعْمَ عُقْبَى الدَّارِ﴾ [الرَّعْدِ: ٢٣، ٢٤] ، وَقَوْلِهِ: ﴿لَا يَسْمَعُونَ فِيهَا لَغْوًا وَلا تَأْثِيمًا * إِلا قِيلا سَلامًا سَلامًا﴾ [الْوَاقِعَةِ: ٢٥، ٢٦] ، فَهُدُوْا إِلَى الْمَكَانِ الَّذِي يَسْمَعُونَ فِيهِ الْكَلَامَ الطَّيِّبَ، ﴿وَيُلَقَّوْنَ فِيهَا تَحِيَّةً وَسَلامًا﴾ [الْفُرْقَانِ: ٧٥] ، لَا كَمَا يُهَانُ أَهْلُ النَّارِ بِالْكَلَامِ الَّذِي يُرَوّعون بِهِ وَيُقَرَّعُونَ بِهِ، يُقَالُ لَهُمْ: ﴿وَذُوقُوا عَذَابَ الْحَرِيقِ﴾

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَهُدُوا إِلَى صِرَاطِ الْحَمِيدِ﴾ أَيْ: إِلَى الْمَكَانِ الَّذِي يَحْمَدُونَ فِيهِ رَبَّهُمْ، عَلَى مَا أَحْسَنَ إِلَيْهِمْ وَأَنْعَمَ بِهِ وَأَسْدَاهُ إِلَيْهِمْ، كَمَا جَاءَ فِي الصَّحِيحِ: "إِنَّهُمْ يُلْهَمُونَ التَّسْبِيحَ وَالتَّحْمِيدَ، كَمَا يُلْهَمُونَ النَّفَسَ".

وَقَدْ قَالَ بَعْضُ الْمُفَسِّرِينَ فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَهُدُوا إِلَى الطَّيِّبِ مِنَ الْقَوْلِ﴾ أَيِ: الْقُرْآنِ. وَقِيلَ: لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ. وَقِيلَ: الْأَذْكَارُ الْمَشْرُوعَةُ، ﴿وَهُدُوا إِلَى صِرَاطِ الْحَمِيدِ﴾ أَيِ: الطَّرِيقِ الْمُسْتَقِيمِ فِي الدُّنْيَا. وَكُلُّ هَذَا لَا يُنَافِي ما ذكرناه، والله أعلم.

---

## 22:25 — verse 25

### Translation

The Exalted says, condemning the disbelievers for their barring the believers from coming to the Sacred Mosque and performing their rites therein, and for their claim that they are its guardians: {And they are not its guardians. Its guardians are only the righteous, but most of them do not know} [al-Anfal: 34].

In this verse there is evidence [that] it is Medinan, just as He said in Surat al-Baqarah: {They ask you about the sacred month, about fighting therein. Say: fighting therein is grave, but barring from the path of God, disbelief in Him, and barring from the Sacred Mosque and expelling its people from it are graver still with God} [al-Baqarah: 217]. And He says here: {Indeed, those who disbelieve and bar from the path of God and from the Sacred Mosque}, meaning: among their characteristics along with their disbelief is that they bar from the path of God and from the Sacred Mosque, that is, they bar from the Sacred Mosque anyone among the believers who intends to go to it, though the believers are in reality the people most entitled to it. This construction in this verse is like His saying: {Those who believe and whose hearts find rest in the remembrance of God. Is it not in the remembrance of God that hearts find rest?} [al-Ra'd: 28], meaning: among their characteristics is that their hearts find rest in the remembrance of God.

Concerning His saying: {which We have made equal for the people, the resident therein and the visitor} [that is, they prevent people from reaching the Sacred Mosque, while God has made it, as a matter of legislated law, equal, with no distinction between the one who resides in it and the one who is far away, distant in dwelling from it. {Equal, the resident therein and the visitor}], among this is the equality of people in the dwellings of Mecca and in residing there. As Ali ibn Abi Talha reported from Ibn Abbas concerning His saying, {equal, the resident therein and the visitor}: he said, the people of Mecca and others alike may stay in the Sacred Mosque.

Mujahid said [concerning His saying]: {equal, the resident therein and the visitor}: the people of Mecca and others are equal in it regarding dwellings. Abu Salih, Abd al-Rahman ibn Sabit, and Abd al-Rahman ibn Zayd [ibn Aslam] said likewise.

Abd al-Razzaq reported from Ma'mar, from Qatadah: its people and those who are not its people are equal in it.

This matter was a point of disagreement between al-Shafi'i and Ishaq ibn Rahwayah at the Mosque of al-Khayf, with Ahmad ibn Hanbal also present. Al-Shafi'i, may God have mercy on him, held that the dwellings of Mecca may be owned, inherited, and rented out, and he cited as evidence the hadith of al-Zuhri, from Ali ibn al-Husayn, from Amr ibn Uthman, from Usamah ibn Zayd, who said: I said, "O Messenger of God, will you stay tomorrow in your house in Mecca?" He said, "Has Aqil left us any dwellings?" Then he said, "The disbeliever does not inherit from the Muslim, nor does the Muslim inherit from the disbeliever." This hadith is recorded in the two Sahihs [and by what is established, that Umar ibn al-Khattab bought a house in Mecca from Safwan ibn Umayyah and made it a prison, for four thousand dirhams. Tawus and Amr ibn Dinar held the same view.

Ishaq ibn Rahwayah held that they may be inherited but not rented out. This is the view of a group among the early generations, and it was stated explicitly by Mujahid and Ata. Ishaq ibn Rahwayah cited as evidence what Ibn Majah reported, from Abu Bakr ibn Abi Shaybah, from Isa ibn Yunus, from Umar ibn Sa'id ibn Abi Husayn, from Uthman ibn Abi Sulayman, from Alqamah ibn Nadlah, who said: The Messenger of God ﷺ died, and Abu Bakr and Umar also died, and] the dwellings of Mecca were never called anything but "the free ones" (al-sawa'ib): whoever needed to dwell there, dwelt there, and whoever had no need, gave others lodging.

Abd al-Razzaq reported from ibn Mujahid, from his father, from Abdullah ibn Amr, that he said: it is not permissible to sell the houses of Mecca nor to rent them out.

He also reported from Ibn Jurayj: Ata used to forbid renting within the sanctuary, and he informed me that Umar ibn al-Khattab used to forbid the fitting of doors on the houses of Mecca, so that pilgrims could stay in their courtyards. The first to fit a door on his house was Suhayl ibn Amr, and Umar ibn al-Khattab sent word to him about this, so he said, "Give me time, O Commander of the Faithful, for I was a merchant, and I wanted to have two doors to secure my goods behind." Umar said, "Very well then."

Abd al-Razzaq reported from Ma'mar, from Mansur, from Mujahid: that Umar ibn al-Khattab said, "O people of Mecca, do not fit doors on your houses, so that the visitor may stay wherever he wishes."

He said: Ma'mar informed us, from one who heard Ata say [concerning His saying]: {equal, the resident therein and the visitor}, he said: they stay wherever they wish.

Al-Daraqutni reported, from the hadith of Ibn Abi Najih, from Abdullah ibn Amr, as a mawquf (halted report): whoever consumes the rent of the houses of Mecca consumes fire.

Imam Ahmad took a middle position [as reported by his son Salih], saying: they may be owned and inherited but not rented out, reconciling the various pieces of evidence. God knows best.

Concerning His saying: {And whoever intends therein deviation through wrongdoing, We will make him taste a painful punishment}, some of the commentators among the grammarians said: the letter ba here is extra, as in His saying: {which grows [with] oil} [al-Mu'minun: 20], meaning: it produces oil. Likewise His saying, {And whoever intends therein deviation}, its sense being "deviation" (without the ba), as al-A'sha said:

"Our spears guaranteed the sustenance of our dependents, between the cooking pots and the bare-necked horse..."

And another poet said:

"In a Yemeni valley whose upper part grows al-shathth, and whose lower part grows al-markh and al-shabahan..."

But it is better to say that the verb here carries the meaning of "to intend" (yahumm), and for this reason it takes the ba as its transitive marker, so He says: {And whoever intends therein deviation through wrongdoing}, meaning: whoever intends therein some grave matter among the major sins.

Concerning His saying: {through wrongdoing}: that is, deliberately, intentionally, knowing that it is wrongdoing, not through misinterpretation, as Ibn Jurayj reported from Ibn Abbas: it means [deliberate intent].

Ali ibn Abi Talha reported from Ibn Abbas: {through wrongdoing} means through shirk (associating partners with God).

Mujahid said: that something other than God be worshipped therein. Qatadah and others said likewise.

Al-Awfi reported from Ibn Abbas: {through wrongdoing} means that you deem permissible within the sanctuary something God has forbidden you, whether through speech or killing, so that you wrong one who has not wronged you, and kill one who has not killed you. When one does that, the painful punishment becomes due [for him].

Mujahid said: {through wrongdoing}: he does an evil deed therein.

This is among the special properties of the sanctuary, that one who merely intends evil within it is punished even if he has not carried it out, as Ibn Abi Hatim said in his tafsir:

[chain] Ahmad ibn Sinan told us, Yazid ibn Harun told us, Shu'bah informed us, from al-Suddi: that he heard Murrah narrate from Abdullah, meaning Ibn Mas'ud, concerning His saying: {And whoever intends therein deviation through wrongdoing}, he said: if a man intended deviation through wrongdoing therein, while he was in Aden Abyan, God would make him taste a painful punishment.

Shu'bah said: he (al-Suddi) raised it to the Prophet ﷺ for us, but I do not raise it for you. Yazid said: he did indeed raise it. Ahmad reported it from Yazid ibn Harun, with the same chain.

[I say: this chain of transmission] is sound according to the criterion of al-Bukhari, though its being a mawquf (halted report) is more fitting than raising it to the Prophet, which is why Shu'bah was firm in holding it to be simply Ibn Mas'ud's own statement. Likewise Asbat and Sufyan al-Thawri reported it from al-Suddi, from Murrah, from Ibn Mas'ud, as a mawquf report. God knows best.

Al-Thawri reported, from al-Suddi, from Murrah, from Abdullah, who said: there is no man who intends an evil deed but it is recorded against him, and if a man in Aden Abyan intended to kill a man at this House, God would make him taste a painful punishment. Al-Dahhak ibn Muzahim said likewise.

Sufyan [al-Thawri] reported, from Mansur, from Mujahid: "deviation therein" is to say, "No, by God," and "Yes indeed, by God" (i.e., false oaths). The same was reported from Mujahid, from Abdullah ibn Amr.

Sa'id ibn Jubayr said: cursing a servant is wrongdoing, and anything beyond that as well.

Sufyan al-Thawri reported, from Abdullah ibn Ata, from Maymun ibn Mihran, from Ibn Abbas concerning His saying: {And whoever intends therein deviation through wrongdoing}, he said: it is the trade of the ruler therein.

From Ibn Umar: selling food [in Mecca] is deviation.

Habib ibn Abi Thabit said, concerning {And whoever intends therein deviation through wrongdoing}: he said: it is the one who hoards goods in Mecca. Others said likewise.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: [chain] Musa ibn Badhan told me, from Ya'la ibn Umayyah, that the Messenger of God ﷺ said: "Hoarding food in Mecca is deviation."

Ibn Abi Hatim said: [chain] Sa'id ibn Jubayr said: Ibn Abbas said concerning the word of God: {And whoever intends therein deviation through wrongdoing}: it was revealed concerning Abdullah ibn Unays. The Messenger of God ﷺ sent him with two men, one an emigrant (muhajir) and the other from the Ansar. They boasted to each other about their lineages, and Abdullah ibn Unays became angry and killed the Ansari man, then apostatized from Islam and fled to Mecca. So this was revealed concerning him: {And whoever intends therein deviation through wrongdoing}, meaning: whoever takes refuge in the sanctuary through deviation, that is, through turning away from Islam.

These reports, although they indicate that these particular things are instances of deviation, the term is in fact more general than that. Rather, they point to something even graver than these. This is why, when the people of the elephant intended to destroy the House, God sent against them flocks of birds {throwing at them stones of baked clay, and He made them like eaten straw} [al-Fil: 4-5], that is, He destroyed them and made them a lesson and a warning to everyone who intends it harm. For this reason it is established in the hadith that the Messenger of God ﷺ said: "An army will march against this House, and when they are at a barren stretch of land, the first of them and the last of them will be swallowed up (by the earth)," the hadith continuing.

Imam Ahmad said: [chain] Ishaq ibn Sa'id, from his father, said: Abdullah ibn Umar came to Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr and said, "O son of al-Zubayr, beware of deviation in the sanctuary of God, for I heard the Messenger of God ﷺ say: 'A man from Quraysh will commit deviation therein, such that if his sins were weighed against the sins of both jinn and mankind, they would outweigh them.' So look to it, that you not be that man."

He also said [in the Musnad of Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As]: [chain] Sa'id ibn Amr said: Abdullah ibn Amr came to Ibn al-Zubayr while he was sitting in the Hijr and said, "O son of al-Zubayr, beware of deviation in the sanctuary, for I bear witness that I heard the Messenger of God ﷺ say: 'A man of Quraysh will make it lawful and will himself become permissible to be fought because of it, and if his sins were weighed against the sins of jinn and mankind, they would outweigh them.'" He said, "So look to it, that you not be that man."

None among the compilers of the hadith collections recorded it through either of these two chains.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ تَعَالَى مُنْكِرًا عَلَى الْكُفَّارِ فِي صَدّهم الْمُؤْمِنِينَ عَنْ إِتْيَانِ الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ، وَقَضَاءِ مَنَاسِكِهِمْ فِيهِ، وَدَعْوَاهُمْ أَنَّهُمُ أَوْلِيَاؤُهُ: ﴿وَمَا كَانُوا أَوْلِيَاءَهُ إِنْ أَوْلِيَاؤُهُ إِلا الْمُتَّقُونَ وَلَكِنَّ أَكْثَرَهُمْ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ﴾ [الْأَنْفَالِ: ٣٤] .

وَفِي هَذِهِ الْآيَةِ دَلِيلٌ [عَلَى] أَنَّهَا مَدَنِيَّةٌ، كَمَا قَالَ فِي سُورَةِ "الْبَقَرَةِ": ﴿يَسْأَلُونَكَ عَنِ الشَّهْرِ الْحَرَامِ قِتَالٍ فِيهِ قُلْ قِتَالٌ فِيهِ كَبِيرٌ وَصَدٌّ عَنْ سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ وَكُفْرٌ بِهِ وَالْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ وَإِخْرَاجُ أَهْلِهِ مِنْهُ أَكْبَرُ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ﴾ [الْبَقَرَةِ: ٢١٧] ، وَقَالَ: هَاهُنَا: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا وَيَصُدُّونَ عَنْ سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ وَالْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ﴾ أَيْ: وَمِنْ صِفَتِهِمْ مَعَ كُفْرِهِمُ أَنَّهُمْ يَصُدُّونَ عَنْ سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ وَالْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ، أَيْ: وَيَصُدُّونَ عَنِ الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ مَنْ أَرَادَهُ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ الَّذِينَ هُمْ أَحَقُّ النَّاسِ بِهِ فِي نَفْسِ الْأَمْرِ، وَهَذَا التَّرْكِيبُ فِي هَذِهِ الْآيَةِ كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَتَطْمَئِنُّ قُلُوبُهُمْ بِذِكْرِ اللَّهِ أَلا بِذِكْرِ اللَّهِ تَطْمَئِنُّ الْقُلُوبُ﴾ [الرَّعْدِ: ٢٨] أَيْ: وَمِنْ صِفَتِهِمُ أَنَّهُمْ تَطْمَئِنُّ قُلُوبُهُمْ بِذِكْرِ اللَّهِ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿الَّذِي جَعَلْنَاهُ لِلنَّاسِ سَوَاءً الْعَاكِفُ فِيهِ وَالْبَادِ﴾ [أَيْ: يَمْنَعُونَ النَّاسَ عَنِ الْوُصُولِ إِلَى الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ، وَقَدْ جَعَلَهُ اللَّهُ شَرْعَا سَوَاءً، لَا فَرْقَ فِيهِ بَيْنَ الْمُقِيمِ فِيهِ وَالنَّائِي عَنْهُ الْبَعِيدِ الدَّارِ مِنْهُ، ﴿سَوَاءً الْعَاكِفُ فِيهِ وَالْبَادِ﴾ ] وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ اسْتِوَاءُ النَّاسِ فِي رِبَاعِ مَكَّةَ وَسُكْنَاهَا، كَمَا قَالَ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَلْحَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿سَوَاءً الْعَاكِفُ فِيهِ وَالْبَادِ﴾ قَالَ: يَنْزِلُ أَهْلُ مَكَّةَ وَغَيْرُهُمْ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ.

وَقَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ [فِي قَوْلِهِ] : ﴿سَوَاءً الْعَاكِفُ فِيهِ وَالْبَادِ﴾ : أَهْلُ مَكَّةَ وَغَيْرُهُمْ فِيهِ سَوَاءٌ فِي الْمَنَازِلِ. وَكَذَا قَالَ أَبُو صَالِحٍ، وَعَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ سَابِطٍ، وَعَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ زَيْدِ [بْنِ أَسْلَمَ] .

وَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ، عَنْ مَعْمَر، عَنْ قَتَادَةَ: سَوَاءٌ فِيهِ أَهْلُهُ وَغَيْرُ أَهْلِهِ.

وَهَذِهِ المسألة اختلف فيها الشافعي وإسحاق بن راهَويه بِمَسْجِدِ الخِيف، وَأَحْمَدُ بْنُ حَنْبَلٍ حَاضِرٌ أَيْضًا، فَذَهَبَ الشَّافِعِيُّ، رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ إِلَى أَنَّ رِبَاعَ مَكَّةَ تُمَلَّكُ وَتُوَرَّثُ وَتُؤَجَّرُ، وَاحْتَجَّ بِحَدِيثِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، عَنْ عَلِيِّ بْنِ الحُسَين، عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ عُثْمَانَ، عَنِ أُسَامَةَ بْنِ زَيْدٍ قَالَ: قُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، أَتَنْزِلُ غَدًا فِي دَارِكَ بِمَكَّةَ؟ فَقَالَ: "وَهَلْ تَرَكَ لَنَا عَقيل مِنْ رِبَاعٍ". ثُمَّ قَالَ: "لَا يَرِثُ الْكَافِرُ الْمُسْلِمَ، وَلَا الْمُسْلِمُ الْكَافِرَ". وَهَذَا الْحَدِيثُ مُخَرّج فِي الصَّحِيحَيْنِ [وَبِمَا ثَبَتَ أَنَّ عُمَرَ بْنَ الْخَطَّابِ اشْتَرَى مِنْ صَفْوَانَ بْنِ أُمَيَّةَ دَارًا بِمَكَّةَ، فَجَعَلَهَا سِجْنًا بِأَرْبَعَةِ آلَافِ دِرْهَمٍ. وَبِهِ قَالَ طَاوُسٌ، وَعَمْرُو بْنُ دِينَارٍ.

وَذَهَبَ إِسْحَاقُ بن راهَويه إلا أَنَّهَا تُوَرَّثُ وَلَا تُؤَجَّرُ. وَهُوَ مَذْهَبُ طَائِفَةٍ من السلف، ونص عليه مجاهد وعطاء، واحتج إسحاق بن راهَويه بِمَا رَوَاهُ ابْنُ مَاجَهْ، عَنْ أَبِي بَكْرِ بْنِ أبي شيبة، عن عيسى ابن يُونُسَ، عَنْ عُمَر بْنِ سَعِيدِ بْنِ أَبِي حُسَين ، عَنْ عُثْمَانَ بْنِ أَبِي سُلَيْمَانَ، عَنْ عَلْقَمَةَ بْنِ نَضْلة قَالَ: تُوُفي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ وَأَبُو بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرُ، وَمَا تُدْعَى رِبَاعُ مَكَّةَ إِلَّا] السَّوَائِبَ، مَنِ احْتَاجَ سَكَنَ، وَمَنِ اسْتَغْنَى أَسْكَنَ .

وَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرزاق ابْنِ مُجَاهِدٍ، عَنِ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو أَنَّهُ قَالَ: لَا يَحِلُّ بَيْعُ دَوْرِ مَكَّةَ وَلَا كِرَاؤُهَا.

وَقَالَ أَيْضًا عَنِ ابْنِ جُرَيْجٍ: كَانَ عَطَاءٌ يَنْهَى عَنِ الْكِرَاءِ فِي الْحَرَمِ، وَأَخْبَرَنِي أَنَّ عُمَرَ بْنَ الْخَطَّابِ كان ينهي عن تُبوّب دُورُ مَكَّةَ؛ لِأَنْ يَنْزِلَ الْحَاجُّ فِي عَرَصاتها، فَكَانَ أَوَّلَ مَنْ بَوّب دَارَهُ سُهَيل بْنُ عَمْرٍو، فَأَرْسَلَ إِلَيْهِ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ فِي ذَلِكَ، فَقَالَ: أَنْظِرْنِي يَا أَمِيرَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ، إِنِّي كُنْتُ امْرَأً تَاجِرًا، فَأَرَدْتُ أَنْ أَتَّخِذَ بَابَيْنِ يَحْبِسَانِ لِي ظَهْرِي قَالَ: فَذَلِكَ إِذًا.

وَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ، عَنْ مَعْمَر، عَنْ مَنْصُورٍ، عَنْ مُجَاهِدٍ؛ أَنَّ عُمَرَ بْنَ الْخَطَّابِ قَالَ: يَا أَهْلَ مَكَّةَ، لَا تَتَّخِذُوا لِدَوْرِكُمْ أَبْوَابًا لِيَنْزِلَ الْبَادِي حَيْثُ يَشَاءُ .

قَالَ: وَأَخْبَرَنَا مَعْمر، عَمَّنْ سَمِعَ عَطَاءً يَقُولُ [فِي قَوْلِهِ] : ﴿سَوَاءً الْعَاكِفُ فِيهِ وَالْبَادِ﴾ ، قَالَ: يَنْزِلُونَ حَيْثُ شَاءُوا.

وَرَوَى الدَّارَقُطْنِيُّ مِنْ حَدِيثِ ابْنِ أَبِي نَجِيح، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو مَوْقُوفًا مَنْ أَكَلَ كِرَاءَ بُيُوتِ مَكَّةَ أَكَلَ نَارًا .

"وَتَوَسَّطَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ [فِيمَا نَقَلَهُ صَالِحٌ ابْنُهُ] فَقَالَ: تُمَلَّكُ وَتُوَرَّثُ وَلَا تُؤَجَّرُ، جَمْعًا بَيْنَ الْأَدِلَّةِ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَمَنْ يُرِدْ فِيهِ بِإِلْحَادٍ بِظُلْمٍ نُذِقْهُ مِنْ عَذَابٍ أَلِيمٍ﴾ قَالَ بَعْضُ الْمُفَسِّرِينَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْعَرَبِيَّةِ: الْبَاءُ هَاهُنَا زَائِدَةٌ، كَقَوْلِهِ: ﴿تَنْبُتُ بِالدُّهْنِ﴾ [الْمُؤْمِنُونَ: ٢٠] أَيْ: تُنْبِتُ الدُّهْنَ، وَكَذَا قَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَمَنْ يُرِدْ فِيهِ بِإِلْحَادٍ ﴾ تَقْدِيرُهُ إِلْحَادًا، وَكَمَا قَالَ الْأَعْشَى:

ضَمنَتْ بِرِزْقِ عِيَالِنَا أرْماحُنا ... بَيْنَ المَرَاجِل، والصّريحَ الْأَجْرَدِ 

وَقَالَ الْآخَرُ:

بوَاد يَمانِ يُنْبتُ الشَّثّ صَدْرُهُ ... وَأسْفَله بالمَرْخ والشَّبَهَان ...

وَالْأَجْوَدُ أَنَّهُ ضَمَّنَ الْفِعْلَ هَاهُنَا مَعْنَى "يَهُمّ"، وَلِهَذَا عَدَّاهُ بِالْبَاءِ، فَقَالَ: ﴿وَمَنْ يُرِدْ فِيهِ بِإِلْحَادٍ بِظُلْمٍ﴾ أَيْ: يَهُمّ فِيهِ بِأَمْرٍ فَظِيعٍ مِنَ الْمَعَاصِي الْكِبَارِ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿بِظُلْمٍ﴾ أَيْ: عَامِدًا قَاصِدًا أَنَّهُ ظُلْمٌ لَيْسَ بِمُتَأَوِّلٍ، كَمَا قَالَ ابْنُ جُرَيْجٍ ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: هُوَ [التَّعَمُّدُ] .

قَالَ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَلْحَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿بِظُلْمٍ﴾ بِشِرْكٍ.

وَقَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ: أَنْ يُعْبَدَ فِيهِ غَيْرُ اللَّهِ. وَكَذَا قَالَ قَتَادَةُ، وَغَيْرُ وَاحِدٍ.

وَقَالَ العَوْفي، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿بِظُلْمٍ﴾ هُوَ أَنْ تَستحلَ مِنَ الْحَرَمِ مَا حَرّم اللَّهُ عَلَيْكَ مِنْ لِسَانٍ أَوْ قَتْلٍ، فَتَظْلِمَ مَنْ لَا يَظْلِمُكَ، وَتَقْتُلَ مَنْ لَا يَقْتُلُكَ، فَإِذَا فَعَلَ ذَلِكَ فَقَدْ وَجَبَ [لَهُ] الْعَذَابُ الْأَلِيمُ.

وَقَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ: ﴿بِظُلْمٍ﴾ : يَعْمَلُ فِيهِ عَمَلًا سَيِّئًا.

وَهَذَا مِنْ خُصُوصِيَّةِ الْحَرَمِ أَنَّهُ يعاقَب الْبَادِي فِيهِ الشَّرَّ، إِذَا كَانَ عَازِمًا عَلَيْهِ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يُوقِعْهُ، كَمَا قَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ فِي تَفْسِيرِهِ:

حَدَّثَنَا أَحْمَدُ بْنُ سِنَان، حَدَّثَنَا يَزِيدُ بْنُ هَارُونَ، أَنْبَأَنَا شُعْبَةُ، عَنِ السُّدِّي: أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ مُرَّة يُحَدِّثُ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ -يَعْنِي ابْنَ مَسْعُودٍ-فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَمَنْ يُرِدْ فِيهِ بِإِلْحَادٍ بِظُلْمٍ﴾ قَالَ: لَوْ أَنَّ رَجُلا أَرَادَ فِيهِ بِإِلْحَادٍ بِظُلْمٍ، وَهُوَ بعَدَن أبينَ، أَذَاقَهُ اللَّهُ مِنَ الْعَذَابِ الْأَلِيمِ.

قَالَ شُعْبَةُ: هُوَ رَفَعَهُ لَنَا، وَأَنَا لَا أَرْفَعُهُ لَكُمْ. قَالَ يَزِيدُ: هُوَ قَدْ رَفَعَهُ، وَرَوَاهُ أَحْمَدُ، عَنْ يَزِيدَ بْنِ هَارُونَ، بِهِ .

[قُلْتُ: هَذَا الْإِسْنَادُ] صَحِيحٌ عَلَى شَرْطِ الْبُخَارِيِّ، وَوَقْفُهُ أَشْبَهُ مِنْ رَفْعِهِ؛ وَلِهَذَا صَمم شُعْبَةُ عَلَى وَقْفه مِنْ كَلَامِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ. وَكَذَلِكَ رَوَاهُ أَسْبَاطٌ، وَسُفْيَانُ الثَّوْرِيُّ، عَنِ السُّدِّيِّ، عَنْ مُرة، عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ مَوْقُوفًا، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

وَقَالَ الثَّوْرِيُّ، عَنِ السُّدِّيُّ، عَنْ مُرَّة، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ قَالَ: مَا مِنْ رَجُلٍ يَهُمُّ بِسَيِّئَةٍ فَتُكْتَبُ عَلَيْهِ، وَلَوْ أَنَّ رَجُلًا بعَدَن أبينَ هَمّ أَنْ يَقْتُلَ رَجُلًا بِهَذَا الْبَيْتِ، لَأَذَاقَهُ اللَّهُ مِنَ الْعَذَابِ الْأَلِيمِ. وَكَذَا قَالَ الضَّحَّاكُ بْنُ مُزاحم.

وَقَالَ سُفْيَانُ [الثَّوْرِيُّ] ، عَنْ مَنْصُورٍ، عَنْ مُجَاهِدٍ "إِلْحَادٌ فِيهِ"، لَا وَاللَّهِ، وَبِلَى وَاللَّهِ. وَرُوِيَ عَنْ مُجَاهِدٍ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو، مثله.

وَقَالَ سَعِيدُ بْنُ جُبَير: شَتْمُ الْخَادِمِ ظُلْمٌ فَمَا فوقَه.

وَقَالَ سُفْيَانُ الثَّوْرِيُّ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَطَاءٍ، عَنْ مَيْمُونُ بْنُ مِهْرَان، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَمَنْ يُرِدْ فِيهِ بِإِلْحَادٍ بِظُلْمٍ﴾ قَالَ: تِجَارَةُ الْأَمِيرِ فِيهِ.

وَعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ: بَيْعُ الطَّعَامِ [بِمَكَّةَ] إِلْحَادٌ.

وَقَالَ حَبِيبُ بْنُ أَبِي ثَابِتٍ: ﴿وَمَنْ يُرِدْ فِيهِ بِإِلْحَادٍ بِظُلْمٍ﴾ قَالَ: الْمُحْتَكِرُ بِمَكَّةَ. وَكَذَا قَالَ غَيْرُ وَاحِدٍ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبِي، حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ إِسْحَاقَ الْجَوْهَرِيُّ، أَنْبَأَنَا أَبُو عَاصِمٍ، عَنْ جَعْفَرِ بْنِ يَحْيَى، عَنْ عَمِّهِ عُمَارَةَ بْنِ ثَوْبَانَ، حَدَّثَنِي مُوسَى بْنُ بَاذَانَ، عَنْ يَعْلَى بْنِ أُمَيَّةَ؛ أن رسولَ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: "احْتِكَارُ الطَّعَامِ بِمَكَّةَ إِلْحَادٌ" .

وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو زُرْعَة، حَدَّثَنَا يَحْيَى بْنُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ بُكَيْر ، حَدَّثَنَا ابْنُ لَهِيعة، حَدَّثَنِي عَطَاءُ بْنُ دِينَارٍ، حَدَّثَنِي سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ قَالَ: قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ فِي قَوْلِ اللَّهِ: ﴿وَمَنْ يُرِدْ فِيهِ بِإِلْحَادٍ بِظُلْمٍ﴾ قَالَ: نَزَلَتْ فِي عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أُنَيْسٍ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وسلم بَعَثَهُ مَعَ رَجُلَيْنِ، أَحَدُهُمَا مُهَاجِرٌ وَالْآخَرُ مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ، فَافْتَخَرُوا فِي الْأَنْسَابِ، فَغَضِبَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ أُنَيْسٍ، فَقَتَلَ الْأَنْصَارِيَّ، ثُمَّ ارْتَدَّ عَنِ الْإِسْلَامِ، وهَرَب إِلَى مَكَّةَ، فَنَزَلَتْ فِيهِ: ﴿وَمَنْ يُرِدْ فِيهِ بِإِلْحَادٍ بِظُلْمٍ﴾ يَعْنِي: مَنْ لَجَأَ إِلَى الْحَرَمِ بِإِلْحَادٍ يَعْنِي بِمَيْلٍ عَنِ الْإِسْلَامِ.

وَهَذِهِ الْآثَارُ، وَإِنْ دَلَّتْ عَلَى أَنَّ هَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاءَ مِنَ الْإِلْحَادِ، ولكنْ هُو أَعَمُّ مِنْ ذَلِكَ، بَلْ فِيهَا تَنْبِيهٌ عَلَى مَا هُوَ أَغْلَظُ مِنْهَا، وَلِهَذَا لَمَّا هَمَّ أَصْحَابُ الْفِيلِ عَلَى تَخْرِيبِ الْبَيْتِ أَرْسَلَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِمْ طَيْرًا أَبَابِيلَ ﴿تَرْمِيهِمْ بِحِجَارَةٍ مِنْ سِجِّيلٍ * فَجَعَلَهُمْ كَعَصْفٍ مَأْكُولٍ﴾ [الْفِيلِ: ٤، ٥] ، أَيْ: دمَّرهم وَجَعَلَهُمْ عِبْرَةً وَنَكَالًا لِكُلِّ مَنْ أَرَادَهُ بِسُوءٍ؛ وَلِذَلِكَ ثَبَتَ فِي الْحَدِيثِ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَالَ: "يَغْزُو هَذَا الْبَيْتَ جَيْشٌ، حَتَّى إِذَا كَانُوا بِبَيْدَاءَ مِنَ الْأَرْضِ خُسِف بِأَوَّلِهِمْ وَآخِرِهِمْ" الْحَدِيثَ .

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ كُنَاسة، حَدَّثَنَا إِسْحَاقُ بْنُ سَعِيدٍ، عَنِ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: أَتَى عبدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ عُمَرَ عبدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ الزُّبَيْرِ، فَقَالَ: يَا ابْنَ الزُّبَيْرِ، إِيَّاكَ وَالْإِلْحَادَ فِي حَرَم اللَّهِ، فَإِنِّي سمعتُ رسولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وسلم يَقُولُ: "إِنَّهُ سيلحدُ فِيهِ رَجُلٌ مَنْ قُرَيْشٍ، لَوْ تُوزَن ذُنُوبُهُ بِذُنُوبِ الثَّقَلَيْنِ لَرَجَحَتْ"، فَانْظُرْ لَا تَكُنْ هُوَ .

وَقَالَ أَيْضًا [فِي مُسْنَدِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرِو بْنِ الْعَاصِ] : حَدَّثَنَا هاشم، حدثنا إسحاق بن سعيد، حَدَّثَنَا سَعِيدُ بْنُ عَمْرٍو قَالَ: أَتَى عبدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ عَمْرٍو ابنَ الزُّبَيْرِ، وَهُوَ جَالِسٌ فِي الحِجْر فَقَالَ: يَا بْنَ الزُّبَيْرِ، إِيَّاكَ والإلحادَ فِي الْحَرَمِ، فَإِنِّي أَشْهَدُ لسَمعتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ يَقُولُ: "يَحِلُّهَا وَيَحِلُّ بِهِ رَجُلٌ مِنْ قُرَيْشٍ، وَلَوْ وُزنت ذُنُوبُهُ بِذُنُوبِ الثَّقَلَيْنِ لَوَزَنَتْهَا". قَالَ: فَانْظُرْ لَا تَكُنْ هُوَ .

وَلَمْ يُخْرِجْهُ أَحَدٌ مِنْ أَصْحَابِ الْكُتُبِ مِنْ هَذَيْنَ الْوَجْهَيْنِ.

---

## 22:26-27 — verses 26-27 (shared commentary)

### Translation

This contains a rebuke and reproach for those among Quraysh who worshipped other than Allah and associated partners with Him, in the very spot which had been established from the first day upon the oneness of Allah and His worship alone, without partner. So the Exalted mentions that He established for Ibrahim the location of the House, meaning: He guided him to it, delivered it to him, and gave him permission to build it.

Many of those who said, "Ibrahim (peace be upon him) is the first to have built the Ancient House, and that it was not built before him," relied on this, as is established in the Sahih from Abu Dharr, who said: I said, "O Messenger of Allah, which mosque was laid down first?" He said, "al-Masjid al-Haram." I said, "Then which?" He said, "Bayt al-Maqdis." I said, "How long between them?" He said, "Forty years."

Allah the Exalted has said: {Indeed, the first House established for mankind is the one at Bakkah, blessed and a guidance for all peoples. In it are clear signs, the station of Ibrahim} [Al Imran: 96, 97], and He the Exalted said: {And We charged Ibrahim and Isma'il, saying: Purify My House for those who circumambulate, those who abide in devotion, and those who bow and prostrate} [al-Baqarah: 125].

We have already presented earlier what has come regarding the building of the House from the sound reports and narrations, in a manner that makes repeating it here unnecessary.

The Exalted says here: {that you not associate anything with Me} meaning: build it upon My name alone, {and purify My House} Mujahid and Qatadah said: from shirk (associating partners), {for those who circumambulate and those who stand and those who bow and prostrate} meaning: make it purely devoted to those who worship Allah alone, without partner.

Circumambulation (tawaf) around it is well known, and it is the most specific act of worship connected to the House, for it is not performed at any spot of the earth besides it. {And those who stand} meaning: in prayer; and for this reason He said: {and those who bow and prostrate}, thereby linking tawaf with prayer, because neither of them is prescribed except as specifically connected to the House. Tawaf is performed at it, and prayer is directed toward it in most circumstances, except for what is excepted regarding prayer when the qiblah direction is uncertain, or during war, or in voluntary prayer while traveling. And Allah knows best.

His saying: {And proclaim to mankind the Hajj} meaning: call out among the people, inviting them to Hajj to this House which We commanded you to build. It is reported that he said: "O my Lord, how shall I make this reach the people when my voice does not carry to them?" It was said to him: "Call out, and the conveying of it is upon Us."

So he stood at his station, it is said upon the Rock, it is said upon al-Safa, it is said upon Abu Qubays, and said: "O people, your Lord has taken a House, so make pilgrimage to it." It is said that the mountains lowered themselves until the voice reached the far corners of the earth, and made those still in wombs and loins hear it, and everything that heard it responded, from stone, clay, and tree, and whoever Allah had decreed would perform Hajj until the Day of Resurrection said: "Labbayka Allahumma labbayk (Here I am, O Allah, here I am)."

This is the substance of what has been reported from Ibn Abbas, Mujahid, Ikrimah, Sa'id ibn Jubayr, and more than one of the salaf (predecessors). And Allah knows best.

Ibn Jarir and Ibn Abi Hatim reported it at length.

His saying: {They will come to you on foot and on every lean camel, coming from every deep mountain pass} Some scholars who held that performing Hajj on foot, for one who is able to do so, is superior to performing Hajj while riding, cite this verse as evidence, because He mentioned the walkers first, which indicates attention to them and the strength of their resolve and the intensity of their determination. But the view held by the majority is that performing Hajj while riding is superior, following the example of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, for he performed Hajj while riding despite the fullness of his strength, upon him be peace.

His saying: {coming from every fajj} means: every path, as He said: {And We made therein passes as ways} [al-Anbiya: 31].

His saying: {'amiq} means: distant. This was said by Mujahid, Ata, al-Suddi, Qatadah, Muqatil ibn Hayyan, al-Thawri, and more than one other.

This verse is like His saying, informing us about Ibrahim, when he said in his supplication: {So make the hearts of some people incline toward them} [Ibrahim: 37]. There is no one among the people of Islam except that he yearns to see the Ka'bah and to perform tawaf around it, and people set out toward it from every direction and every region.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

هَذَا فِيهِ تَقْرِيعٌ وَتَوْبِيخٌ لِمَنْ عَبَدَ غَيْرَ اللَّهِ، وَأَشْرَكَ بِهِ مِنْ قُرَيْشٍ، فِي الْبُقْعَةِ الَّتِي أسسّتْ مِنْ أَوَّلِ يَوْمٍ عَلَى تَوْحِيدِ اللَّهِ وَعِبَادَتِهِ وَحْدَهُ لَا شَرِيكَ لَهُ، فَذَكَرَ تَعَالَى أَنَّهُ بَوأ إِبْرَاهِيمَ مكانَ الْبَيْتِ، أَيْ: أَرْشَدَهُ إِلَيْهِ، وَسَلَّمَهُ لَهُ، وَأَذِنَ لَهُ فِي بِنَائِهِ.

وَاسْتَدَلَّ بِهِ كَثِيرٌ مِمَّنْ قَالَ: "إِنَّ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، هُوَ أَوَّلُ مَنْ بَنَى الْبَيْتَ الْعَتِيقَ، وَأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُبْنَ قَبْلَهُ"، كَمَا ثَبَتَ فِي الصَّحِيحِ عَنِ أَبِي ذَرٍّ قُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، أَيُّ مَسْجِدٍ وُضعَ أَوَّلُ؟ قَالَ: "الْمَسْجِدُ الْحَرَامُ". قُلْتُ: ثُمَّ أَيُّ؟ قَالَ: "بَيْتُ الْمَقْدِسِ". قُلْتُ كَمْ بَيْنَهُمَا؟ قَالَ: "أَرْبَعُونَ سَنَةً" .

وَقَدْ قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: ﴿إِنَّ أَوَّلَ بَيْتٍ وُضِعَ لِلنَّاسِ لَلَّذِي بِبَكَّةَ مُبَارَكًا وَهُدًى لِلْعَالَمِينَ. فِيهِ آيَاتٌ بَيِّنَاتٌ مَقَامُ إِبْرَاهِيم﴾ الْآيَةَ [آلِ عِمْرَانَ: ٩٦، ٩٧] ، وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَعَهِدْنَا إِلَى إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَإِسْمَاعِيلَ أَنْ طَهِّرَا بَيْتِيَ لِلطَّائِفِينَ وَالْعَاكِفِينَ وَالرُّكَّعِ السُّجُودِ﴾ [الْبَقَرَةِ: ١٢٥] .

وَقَدْ قَدَّمْنَا ذِكْرَ مَا وَرَدَ فِي بِنَاءِ الْبَيْتِ مِنَ الصِّحَاحِ وَالْآثَارِ، بِمَا أَغْنَى عَنِ إِعَادَتِهِ هَاهُنَا .

وَقَالَ تَعَالَى هَاهُنَا: ﴿أَنْ لَا تُشْرِكْ بِي﴾ أَيِ: ابْنه عَلَى اسْمِي وَحْدِي، ﴿وَطَهِّرْ بَيْتِيَ﴾ قَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ وَقَتَادَةُ: مِنَ الشِّرْكِ، ﴿لِلطَّائِفِينَ وَالْقَائِمِينَ وَالرُّكَّعِ السُّجُودِ﴾ أَيِ: اجْعَلْهُ خَالِصًا لِهَؤُلَاءِ الَّذِينَ يَعْبُدُونَ اللَّهَ وَحْدَهُ لَا شَرِيكَ لَهُ.

فَالطَّائِفُ بِهِ مَعْرُوفٌ، وَهُوَ أَخَصُّ الْعِبَادَاتِ عِنْدَ الْبَيْتِ، فَإِنَّهُ لَا يُفْعَلُ بِبُقْعَةٍ مِنَ الْأَرْضِ سِوَاهَا، ﴿وَالْقَائِمِينَ﴾ أَيْ: فِي الصَّلَاةِ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿وَالرُّكَّعِ السُّجُودِ﴾ فَقَرَنَ الطَّوَافَ بِالصَّلَاةِ؛ لِأَنَّهُمَا لَا يُشْرَعَانِ إِلَّا مُخْتَصَّيْنِ بِالْبَيْتِ، فَالطَّوَافُ عِنْدَهُ، وَالصَّلَاةُ إِلَيْهِ فِي غَالِبِ الْأَحْوَالِ، إِلَّا مَا اسْتُثْنِيَ مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ عِنْدَ اشْتِبَاهِ الْقِبْلَةِ وَفِي الْحَرْبِ، وَفِي النَّافِلَةِ فِي السِّفْرِ، وَاللَّهُ أعلم.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَأَذِّنْ فِي النَّاسِ بِالْحَجِّ﴾ أَيْ: نَادِ فِي النَّاسِ دَاعِيًا لَهُمُ إِلَى الْحَجِّ إِلَى هَذَا الْبَيْتِ الَّذِي أَمَرْنَاكَ بِبِنَائِهِ. فَذُكر أَنَّهُ قَالَ: يَا رَبِّ، وَكَيْفَ أُبْلِغُ النَّاسَ وَصَوْتِي لَا يَنْفُذُهُمْ؟ فَقِيلَ: نَادِ وَعَلَيْنَا الْبَلَاغُ.

فَقَامَ عَلَى مَقَامِهِ، وَقِيلَ: عَلَى الْحَجَرِ، وَقِيلَ: عَلَى الصَّفَا، وَقِيلَ: عَلَى أَبِي قُبَيس، وَقَالَ: يَا أَيُّهَا النَّاسُ، إِنْ رَبَّكُمْ قَدِ اتَّخَذَ بَيْتًا فَحُجُّوهُ، فَيُقَالُ: إِنَّ الْجِبَالَ تَوَاضَعَتْ حَتَّى بَلَغَ الصَّوْتُ أَرْجَاءَ الْأَرْضِ، وأسمَعَ مَن فِي الْأَرْحَامِ وَالْأَصْلَابِ، وَأَجَابَهُ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ سَمِعَهُ مِنْ حَجَر ومَدَر وَشَجَرٍ، وَمَنْ كَتَبَ اللَّهُ أَنَّهُ يَحُجُّ إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ: "لَبَّيْكَ اللَّهُمَّ لَبَّيْكَ".

هَذَا مَضْمُونُ مَا رُوِيَ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، وَمُجَاهِدٍ، وَعِكْرِمَةَ، وَسَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَير، وَغَيْرِ وَاحِدٍ مِنَ السَّلَفِ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

أَوْرَدَهَا ابْنُ جَرير، وَابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ مُطَوّلة .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿يَأْتُوكَ رِجَالا وَعَلَى كُلِّ ضَامِرٍ يَأْتِينَ مِنْ كُلِّ فَجٍّ عَمِيقٍ﴾ قَدْ يَستدلّ بِهَذِهِ الْآيَةِ مَنْ ذَهَبَ مِنَ الْعُلَمَاءِ إِلَى أَنَّ الْحَجَّ مَاشِيًا، لِمَنْ قَدَرَ عَلَيْهِ، أفضلُ مِنَ الْحَجِّ رَاكِبًا؛ لِأَنَّهُ قَدَّمَهُمْ فِي الذِّكْرِ، فَدَلَّ عَلَى الِاهْتِمَامِ بِهِمْ وَقُوَّةِ هِمَمِهِمْ وَشِدَّةِ عَزْمِهِمْ، وَالَّذِي عَلَيْهِ الْأَكْثَرُونَ أَنَّ الْحَجَّ رَاكِبًا أَفْضَلُ؛ اقْتِدَاءً بِرَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ، فَإِنَّهُ حَجَّ رَاكِبًا مَعَ كَمَالِ قُوَّتِهِ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿يَأْتِينَ مِنْ كُلِّ فَجٍّ﴾ يَعْنِي: طَرِيقٍ، كَمَا قَالَ: ﴿وَجَعَلْنَا فِيهَا فِجَاجًا سُبُلا﴾ [الْأَنْبِيَاءِ: ٣١] .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿عَمِيقٍ﴾ أَيْ: بَعِيدٍ. قَالَهُ مُجَاهِدٌ، وَعَطَاءٌ، وَالسُّدِّيُّ، وَقَتَادَةُ، وَمُقَاتِلُ بْنُ حَيَّانَ، وَالثَّوْرِيُّ، وَغَيْرُ وَاحِدٍ.

وَهَذِهِ الْآيَةُ كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى إِخْبَارًا عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، حَيْثُ قَالَ فِي دُعَائِهِ: ﴿فَاجْعَلْ أَفْئِدَةً مِنَ النَّاسِ تَهْوِي إِلَيْهِمْ﴾ [إِبْرَاهِيمَ: ٣٧] فَلَيْسَ أَحَدٌ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْإِسْلَامِ إِلَّا وَهُوَ يَحِنُّ إِلَى رُؤْيَةِ الْكَعْبَةِ وَالطَّوَافِ، فَالنَّاسُ يَقْصِدُونَهَا مِنْ سَائِرِ الْجِهَاتِ وَالْأَقْطَارِ.

---

## 22:28-29 — verses 28-29 (shared commentary)

### Translation

Ibn Abbas said regarding {so that they may witness benefits for themselves}: he said: the benefits of this world and the next. As for the benefits of the next world, they are God's good pleasure, and as for the benefits of this world, they are what they attain of the benefits of the sacrificial animals, of profit, and of trade. Mujahid and several others said likewise: that it refers to the benefits of this world and the next, similar to His saying: {There is no blame upon you in seeking bounty from your Lord} [al-Baqarah: 198].

Regarding His statement: {and mention the name of God [during known days] over what He has provided for them of grazing livestock}, Shu'bah [and Hushaym] reported from [Abu Bishr, from Sa'id], from Ibn Abbas: the known days are the ten days. Al-Bukhari cited this from him in a form of definite attribution. A similar report is transmitted from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, Mujahid, Ata, Sa'id ibn Jubayr, al-Hasan, Qatadah, al-Dahhak, Ata al-Khurasani, and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. This is the position of al-Shafi'i and the well-known view of Ahmad ibn Hanbal.

Al-Bukhari said: [chain] Muhammad ibn Ar'arah, Shu'bah, Sulayman, Muslim al-Batin, Sa'id ibn Jubayr, from Ibn Abbas, from the Prophet ﷺ, who said: "There are no days in which deeds are more excellent than in these." They said: "Not even jihad in the path of God?" He said: "Not even jihad in the path of God, except a man who goes out risking his life and his wealth and does not return with anything."

It was also related by Imam Ahmad, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah. Al-Tirmidhi said: a hasan (sound), gharib (singular), sahih (authentic) hadith. On this subject there are also reports from Ibn Umar, Abu Hurayrah, Abdullah ibn Amr, and Jabir.

I say: I have thoroughly traced these transmission paths and have devoted a separate volume to them. Among these is what Imam Ahmad reported: [chain] Affan, Abu Awanah, Yazid ibn Abi Ziyad, from Mujahid, from Ibn Umar, who said: the Messenger of God ﷺ said: "There are no days greater before God, nor is deed more beloved to Him therein, than in these ten days, so increase during them in tahlil (proclaiming there is no god but God), takbir (proclaiming God's greatness), and tahmid (praising God)." It is also related through another route from Mujahid, from Ibn Umar, in similar wording. Al-Bukhari said: Ibn Umar and Abu Hurayrah used to go out to the marketplace during the ten days and proclaim takbir, and the people would proclaim takbir following their example.

Ahmad related from Jabir, as a raised report (marfu'), that this is the ten referred to in God's oath: {By the dawn, and by ten nights} [al-Fajr: 1-2].

Some of the early scholars said that this is what is meant by His words: {and We completed it with ten} [al-A'raf: 142].

In the Sunan of Abu Dawud it is established that the Messenger of God ﷺ used to fast during these ten days.

These ten days include the Day of Arafah, concerning which it is established in Sahih Muslim, from Abu Qatadah, who said: the Messenger of God ﷺ was asked about fasting on the Day of Arafah, and he said: "I anticipate from God that it will expiate the sins of the past year and the coming year."

They also include the Day of Sacrifice (Yawm al-Nahr), which is the Day of the Greater Pilgrimage. It has come in a hadith that it is the most excellent of days before God.

In sum, it has been said that these ten days are the most excellent days of the year, as the hadith states, and many have given them preference over the last ten days of Ramadan, since whatever is prescribed in the latter, such as fasting, prayer, charity, and the like, is also prescribed in these, while these ten days have the distinction of the obligatory Hajj being performed within them.

It has also been said that the last ten of Ramadan are more excellent because they contain the Night of Decree (Laylat al-Qadr), which is better than a thousand months.

Others took a middle position and said: the days of these ten (of Dhul-Hijjah) are more excellent, and the nights of those ten (of Ramadan) are more excellent. By this, the various evidences are reconciled. And God knows best.

A second opinion regarding the known days: al-Hakam, from Miqsam, from Ibn Abbas: the known days are the Day of Sacrifice and the three days following it. This is also related from Ibn Umar and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, and it is the view Ahmad ibn Hanbal adopted in one report from him.

A third opinion: Ibn Abi Hatim said: [chain] my father, Ali ibn al-Madini, Yahya ibn Sa'id, Ibn Ajlan, told me Nafi', that Ibn Umar used to say: the known days and the counted days together total four days. The known days are the Day of Sacrifice and the two days following it, and the counted days are the three days following the Day of Sacrifice.

This chain of transmission back to him is sound, and al-Suddi said the same. This is the position of Imam Malik ibn Anas. This opinion, and the one before it, are supported by God's statement: {over what He has provided for them of grazing livestock}, meaning: the mention of God's name at the time of their slaughter.

A fourth opinion: that they are the Day of Arafah, the Day of Sacrifice, and one more day after it. This is the position of Abu Hanifah.

Ibn Wahb said: Ibn Zayd ibn Aslam told me, from his father, that he said: the known days are the Day of Arafah, the Day of Sacrifice, and the days of Tashriq.

Regarding His statement: {over what He has provided for them of grazing livestock}, it means: camels, cattle, and sheep, as God detailed them in Surat al-An'am, and that they are {eight kinds in pairs} [al-An'am: 143].

Regarding His statement: {So eat of it and feed the distressed, the poor}, some who held that eating from the sacrificial animals is obligatory relied on this verse. This is a rare, unusual opinion. The majority hold that it belongs to the category of permission or of what is merely recommended, as it is established that when the Messenger of God ﷺ slaughtered his sacrificial animals, he ordered that a piece from each camel be taken and cooked, then he ate of its meat and sipped of its broth.

Abdullah ibn Wahb said: [Malik told me: I like for a person to eat from his sacrifice, because God says: {So eat of it}. Ibn Wahb said:] and I asked al-Layth, and he told me the same.

Sufyan al-Thawri, from Mansur, from Ibrahim, regarding {So eat of it}: he said: the polytheists used not to eat from their sacrifices, so permission was granted to the Muslims: whoever wishes may eat, and whoever wishes may abstain. A similar report is related from Mujahid and Ata.

Hushaym said, from Husayn, from Mujahid, regarding His statement {So eat of it}: it is like His statement: {and when you are free from the restrictions of pilgrim sanctity, then hunt} [al-Ma'idah: 2], and {then when the prayer is concluded, disperse throughout the land} [al-Jumu'ah: 10].

This is the view adopted by Ibn Jarir in his tafsir. Those who supported the opinion that half of the sacrificial animal should be given away in charity relied on His statement in this verse: {So eat of it and feed the distressed, the poor}, dividing it into two halves: half for the one offering the sacrifice, and half for the poor.

The other opinion is that it should be divided into three parts: a third for himself, a third that he gives as a gift, and a third that he gives in charity, based on His statement in the other verse: {So eat of it and feed the needy who is content and the needy who asks} [al-Hajj: 36]. Discussion of this will come at its place, God willing, and in Him is trust.

Regarding His statement {the distressed, the poor}: Ikrimah said: he is the one in dire need upon whom distress has fallen, [and the poor person] is the one who refrains from asking.

Mujahid said: he is the one who does not extend his hand (asking). Qatadah said: he is the chronically ill. Muqatil ibn Hayyan said: he is the blind person.

Regarding His statement: {then let them complete their tafath}: Ali ibn Abi Talhah, from Ibn Abbas: it is the removal of the state of pilgrim sanctity through shaving the head, wearing regular clothes, cutting the nails, and the like. Ata and Mujahid related this likewise from him. Ikrimah and Muhammad ibn Ka'b al-Qurazi said the same.

Ikrimah, from Ibn Abbas, said regarding {then let them complete their tafath}: he said: tafath refers to the rites of pilgrimage.

Regarding His statement: {and let them fulfill their vows}: Ali ibn Abi Talhah, from Ibn Abbas: it means: the slaughter of what one has vowed of sacrificial animals.

Ibn Abi Najih, from Mujahid: {and let them fulfill their vows}: the vow of Hajj and of the sacrificial offering, and whatever a person has vowed that is connected with the Hajj.

Ibrahim ibn Maysarah, from Mujahid, said regarding {and let them fulfill their vows}: he said: sacrificial animals.

Layth ibn Abi Sulaym, from Mujahid: {and let them fulfill their vows}: every vow with a set term.

Ikrimah said regarding {and let them fulfill their vows}: he said: [their Hajj.

Imam Ibn Abi Hatim likewise related: [chain] my father, Ibn Abi Umar, Sufyan, regarding His statement {and let them fulfill their vows}: he said:] the vow of Hajj, for everyone who enters into the Hajj must perform the rites required of him therein: circling the House, going between al-Safa and al-Marwah, standing at Arafah, at Muzdalifah, and casting the pebbles, according to what they have been commanded. A similar view is related from Malik.

Regarding His statement: {and circle the ancient House}: Mujahid said: it means the obligatory circumambulation performed on the Day of Sacrifice.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: [chain] Abu Hamza said: Ibn Abbas said to me: Do you recite Surat al-Hajj? God says: {And let them circumambulate the Ancient House}, for indeed the last of the rites is circumambulation of the House.

I say: this is what the Messenger of God ﷺ did, for when he returned to Mina on the Day of Sacrifice, he began by casting the pebbles at the jamra, throwing seven pebbles at it, then he sacrificed his offering, then shaved his head, then he proceeded and circumambulated the House. And in the Sahih, from Ibn Abbas, he said: the people were commanded that the last thing they do regarding the House should be circumambulation, except that this was lightened for the menstruating woman.

Regarding His saying, {the Ancient House}: in this there is evidence for those who hold that circumambulation must be performed behind al-Hijr, because it is part of the original structure of the House that Ibrahim (peace be upon him) built, even though Quraysh had excluded it from the House when their funds fell short.
